It can be reasonably asserted that R&D efforts will be extensive in industries where key technologies are judged to have high potential for further development, and less so when technological prospects appear to be limited. Firms in traditional industries like food and primary metals typically devote only 0.4 percent of their sales revenues to R&D, while firms in the pharmaceutical industry may spend 16 to 20 percent of their revenues on R&D. 试图精确衡量组织规模与发明活动之间联系的努力得到了参半的结果。大型组织在技术进步过程中发挥卓越作用的架设没有得到支持，但也没有被完全否定。试图在公司规模和发明活动之间找到简单的相关性（正或负）注定会失败，因为必须考虑规模以外的因素。至少同样重要的是与行业产品和运营相关的技术的感知发展潜力。可以合理地推断，在关键技术被认为具有很大进一步发展潜力的行业中，研发工作将广泛进行，而在技术前景似乎有限的行业中则较少。食品和初级金属等传统行业的公司通常仅将销售收入的 0.4% 用于研发，而制药行业的公司可能会将其收入的 16% 至 20% 用于研发。
Even if a correlation between size and inventive activity existed, it would tell us nothing about how effective the research efforts of large firms have been. In fact, it is likely that small firms do a better job of producing new technologies relative to the cost of their research expenditures. Moreover, much of the research conducted by large organizations with secure markets is not oriented toward the production of radically new things but is directed at the creation of modest improvements.Much of it is simply defensive and imitative. Large firms that control a substantial share of their market are more likely to produce inventions that maintain the status quo and to avoid engaging in research that might radically alter the industry in which they already have a comfortable niche. Conversely, small firms or independent units of larger firms have been more successful in creating, developing, and marketing inventions that disrupt the technological status quo. 即使规模和发明活动之间存在相关性，它也不能告诉我们大公司的研究工作有多有效。 事实上，相对于研究支出的成本，小公司可能在生产新技术方面做得更好。 此外，拥有安全市场的大型组织进行的大部分研究并不面向全新事物的生产，而是进行适度的改进。 其中大部分只是防御性和模仿性的。 控制大量市场份额的大公司更有可能创造维持现状的发明，并避免参与可能从根本上改变他们已经拥有舒适利基行业的研究。 相反，小公司或大公司的独立单位在创造、开发和营销破坏技术现状的发明方面更为成功。
To be sure, invention is not the same thing as innovation. To actually bring an invention successfully into the marketplace may require the resources of a large organization. As we have already seen, the development of new technologies can be a lengthy and expensive process. Large organizations are often better equipped to do development work, where scaling up and making relatively small but nonetheless crucial improvements are the key tasks. This may be their most important contribution to technological innovation. Even so, gigantic size does not appear to be necessary or even beneficial. Large size may be necessary to muster the resources necessary for effective development work, but past a threshold size there appear to be no advantages to bigness. 可以肯定的是，发明与创新不同。 要将一项发明真正成功地推向市场，可能需要大型组织的资源。 正如我们已经看到的，新技术的开发可能是一个漫长而昂贵的过程。 大型组织通常更有能力进行开发工作，其中扩大规模和进行相对较小但仍然至关重要的改进是关键任务。 这可能是他们对技术创新最重要的贡献。 即便如此，巨大的规模并不总是必要，甚至可能适得其反。 大尺寸可能可以用来聚集有效开发工作所需的资源，但超过阈值尺寸似乎没有带来更多的优势。
These generalizations of course do not apply to all industries. In some industries such as nuclear power, the bulk of both the research and development work has been done by large firms and government agencies. In other industries, such as smartphone and tablet apps, a great amount of innovative effort has come from individuals and small firms. About the safest statement that can be made is that technological advance requires the efforts of a wide variety of organizational types and sizes. The initiation and development of some technologies require the massive efforts that only large organizations can provide. At the same time, many technologies have been—and will continue to be—the result of the efforts of people working in small organizations or just by themselves. 当然，这些概括并不适用于所有行业。 在核电等一些行业，大部分研发工作都是由大公司和政府机构完成的。 在其他行业，例如智能手机和平板电脑应用程序，大量的创新努力来自个人和小公司。 可以做出的最保险的声明是技术进步需要各种类型和规模的组织的努力。 一些技术的启动和发展需要大量的努力，只有大型组织才能提供。 与此同时，许多技术已经——并将继续——是在小型组织中工作的人们或仅靠他们自己努力的结果。
Entrepreneurs and Organizations 企业家和组织
Organizations are essential for the operation of established technological systems like airlines or an oil refineries. Their fundamental purpose is to coordinate the efforts of individuals in order to accomplish essential tasks. When routine tasks are involved, this coordination is usually accomplished through the application of basic bureaucratic principles: specialization, formalization (the use of rules, regulations, and standard operating procedures), and hierarchical authority. Although bureaucracies are sometimes thought to be inherently inefficient, there is no reason that they should be. In fact, when it works as it should, a bureaucracy is like a well-oiled machine that faithfully does the job for which it was intended. 组织对于航空公司或炼油厂等成熟技术系统的运营至关重要。 它们的根本目的是协调个人努力以完成基本任务。 当涉及日常任务时，这种协调常常是通过基础的官僚主义原则来完成的：专业化、正规化（使用规则、法规和标准操作程序）和等级权力。 尽管官僚机构有时被认为在本质上效率低下，但没有理由认为它们总是如此。 事实上，当它正常运作时，官僚机构就像一台运转良好的机器，忠实地完成其预期的工作。
But bureaucratic organization has its limitations. As has been noted above, bureaucracies thrive on routine, working best in stable environments where nothing new comes along to disturb their machinelike operations. At the same time, however, these bureaucratic routines are difficult or impossible to reconcile with the inherent uncertainty of creating something new. Furthermore, many unresolved issues surround not just the technology itself but also all of the ancillary changes that may be required to use it effectively. All sorts of uncertainties may be involved in such matters as the acceptance of the technology by customers, the retraining of personnel, legal liabilities, performance of component suppliers, and changing government regulations. 但官僚组织有其局限性。 如上所述，官僚机构发端于例行公事之中，在稳定的环境中最为有效，在这样的环境中没有新的东西干扰他们机械般的运转。 然而，与此同时，这些官僚组织很难或不可能与发明创新的内在不确定性相协调。 此外，许多未解决的问题不仅围绕在技术本身，还围绕在与之配套的可能需要的其它变化上。 客户对技术的接受程度、人员的再培训、法律责任、零部件供应商的表现、政府法规的变化等，都可能涉及各种不确定因素。
Bureaucracies rely on rules, regulations, and formal methods of management to get their employees to do what needs to be done. In most cases, activities and projects are closely scheduled and subject to careful financial scrutiny. But innovators usually need a lot of elbow room and have an indefinite time horizon, which puts them at odds with bureaucratic procedures. A large corporation that is organized according to bureaucratic principles can be a difficult environment for inventors. As Jack Kilby, the co-inventor of the integrated circuit, has noted: "There is a basic incompatibility of the inventor and the large corporation. Large companies have well-developed planning mechanisms which need to know at the beginning of a new project how much it will cost, how long it will take, and above all what it's going to do. None of these answers may be apparent to the inventor." 官僚机构依靠规章制度和正规的管理方法来让员工做他们需要做的事。 在大多数情况下，活动和项目都是紧密安排的，并受到审慎的财务审查。 但是创新者通常需要大量的容错空间和不定的时间范围，这使他们与官僚程序不匹配。 根据官僚主义原则组织的大公司对发明家来说可能是一个痛苦的环境。 正如集成电路的共同发明人 Jack Kilby 所指出的那样："发明者和大公司之间存在着根本的不兼容。 大公司拥有完善的计划机制，需要在新项目开始时就知道它的成本是多少，需要多长时间，最重要的是它要做什么。 对于发明者来说，这些问题中没有一个有显而易见的答案。"
As we have seen in Chapter 3, technological innovation is often the work of entrepreneurs. By definition, entrepreneurs are people who disrupt normal activities and procedures by vigorously pushing new ways of doing things. Promoting innovation is risky business, and routine-seeking bureaucratic organizations are generally disinclined to take risks. Not only is a bureaucracy's structure attuned to routine activities, its personnel usually seek to protect their positions and maintain their customary way of life. Under these circumstances, an entrepreneur's efforts to promote innovation within an organization may encounter a fair amount of resistance and even hostility. 正如我们在第 3 章中看到的，技术创新通常是企业家的工作。 根据定义，企业家是通过推动新的行为方式来破坏正常活动和程序的人。 创新是有风险的事，追求常规的官僚组织通常不愿意承担风险。 官僚机构的结构不仅要适应日常活动，而且其人员通常会寻求保护自己的职位并维持他们的习惯生活方式。 在这种情况下，企业家在组织内推动创新的努力可能会遇到相当多的阻力甚至敌意。
Although entrepreneurial activities are usually associated with the private sector, entrepreneurship may emerge as a force for change in government agencies, charitable organizations, schools, and religious institutions. The transformative power of an entrepreneur in the face of stiff opposition is well illustrated by an episode in the history of one of the most hidebound institutions in nineteenth-century America, the U.S. Navy. At that time, gunnery was highly inaccurate; of the 9,500 shots fired from American naval vessels during the Spanish-American War, only 121 found their target. No attempt was made to follow a target; gunners used their cannons' elevating gear to give the shell the proper trajectory, fired after the roll of the ship brought the target into their sights, and hoped for the best. Then, during the last years of the nineteenth century, a British naval officer modified the elevating gear of his ship's guns so that they could be rapidly moved, allowing them to continuously track their target. He also modified the gun's telescopic sight so that it wouldn't poke the gunner in the eye when the gun recoiled. 尽管创业活动通常与私营部门有关，但企业家精神可能会成为改变政府机构、慈善组织、学校和宗教机构的力量。 19 世纪美国最隐蔽的机构之一，美国海军的历史插曲很好地说明了企业家在面对强烈反对时的变革力量。当时，炮弹是极不精准的；在美西战争期间美国海军舰艇发射的 9,500 发炮弹中，只有 121 发射中了目标。没有试图瞄准目标；炮手使用大炮的升降装置为炮弹提供大概的轨道，在船的横摇中等待目标进入他们的视野，之后便全凭运气开火。然后，在 19 世纪的最后几年，一位英国海军军官改装了他舰上火炮的升降装置，使其能够快速移动，从而能够持续跟踪目标。他还修改了枪的望远镜瞄准器，以便在枪后座时它不会戳到炮手的眼睛。
The improvements in accuracy were spectacular, and before long an American officer named William S. Sims embarked on a personal mission to bring these improvements to American ships. Sims was the quintessential entrepreneur; although he hadn't invented the new system, he was utterly convinced of its value and passionately devoted to seeing it installed. And he was willing to rattle a lot of cages in the course of promoting it. For its part, the Navy acted as a bureaucracy might be expected to act. At first, it ignored Sims' reports on the inadequacies of American gunnery technology and what could be done to improve it. The reports were simply filed away, where they provided a few good meals for the cockroaches that inhabited the file cabinets. When Sims became too insistent to be ignored, the Navy arranged a series of inappropriate tests that "proved" the inadequacy of the new system. Sims finally prevailed only after he succeeded in getting the attention of President Theodore Roosevelt, who installed him in a position that allowed him ultimately to become "the man who taught the Navy to shoot." 精准度的提高十分显著，不久之后，一位名叫威廉 S. 西姆斯(William S. Sims)的美国军官开始执行一项个人任务：将这些改进带到美国舰艇上。西姆斯是典型的企业家；虽然他当时还没有发明新系统，但他完全相信它的前景，并热切地致力将其付诸实践。而且在推广的过程中，他并不担心得罪人。就其本身而言，海军充当了一个可能会采取行动的官僚机构。起初，它忽略了西姆斯关于美国枪炮技术不足以及可以做些什么来改进它的报告。报告被简单地归档了，在那里它们为栖息在文件柜中的蟑螂提供了几顿好饭。当西姆斯变得过于坚持而不能被忽视时，海军安排了一系列不恰当的测试来"证明"新系统的不足。西姆斯在成功引起西奥多·罗斯福(Theodore Roosevelt)总统的注意后终于占了上风，罗斯福总统让他最终成为"教育美国海军射击的人"。
The case of Sims versus the United States Navy is an admittedly extreme example of conflict between an entrepreneur and an entrenched bureaucracy. There are, after all, many examples of successful working relationships between innovative individuals and the organizations that employ them. Not every organization is structured along classic bureaucratic lines, and as we have already seen, an organization committed to innovation will likely have different structural characteristics than one pursuing routine activities. Still, there is no getting around the fact that organizations may find it hard to accommodate employees who take on the role of entrepreneur. These individuals can be arrogant, stubborn, and single-minded to the point of fanaticism. But at the same time, their vision and energy may be the most important element in their organization's success. To take a recent example, Steve Jobs embodied the positive and negative qualities of the classic entrepreneur. He was an exceedingly difficult person in many ways, but without his vision and guidance Apple Computer would lie buried along with the dozens of defunct personal computer firms that are barely remembered today. 西姆斯与美国海军的案子是企业家和根深蒂固的官僚机构之间​​冲突的一个公认的极端例子。毕竟，创新的个人和雇佣他们的组织之间有很多成功的工作关系的例子。并非每个组织都按照经典的官僚路线构建，正如我们已经看到的，致力于创新的组织可能具有与追求日常活动的组织不同的结构特征。尽管如此，组织可能会发现很难容纳扮演企业家角色的员工，这一事实仍然无法回避。这些人可能傲慢、固执、一心一意到狂热的地步。但与此同时，他们的愿景和精力可能是他们组织成功的最重要因素。举一个最近的例子，史蒂夫乔布斯(Steve Jobs)体现了企业家典型的正面和负面特质。他在很多方面都是一个非常强硬的人，但如果没有他的远见和指导，苹果电脑将与今天几乎不为人知的数十家已倒闭的个人电脑公司一起被埋葬。
For many organizations, technological dynamism has required continual efforts to find a balance between the needs of would-be entrepreneurs and established organizational structures and processes. We cannot discard bureaucratic organizations, but we need to find ways that allow them to continue doing what they do best, while at the same time preventing them from obstructing the individuals whose efforts are a major source of technological advance. 对于许多组织而言，技术活力需要不断在潜在企业家的需求与已建立的组织结构和流程之间找到平衡。 我们不能抛弃官僚组织，但我们需要想办法让他们继续做他们最擅长的事情，同时防止他们阻碍那些努力成为技术进步主要来源的个人。
Complex societies could not exist without organizations, bureaucratic or otherwise. Organizations are no less important for the initiation, development, and application of most technologies. At the same time, however, inappropriate organizational structures can stifle technological advance. Equally important, the controllers of powerful organizations can select and cultivate technologies that serve only their own interests. This problem is not confined to business organizations; it can also manifest itself in the public sector. Accordingly, we will turn our attention to the biggest and potentially most powerful organization of all: the federalgovernment. 没有组织、官僚或其他组织，复杂的社会就不可能存在。 对于大多数技术的启动、开发和应用，组织同样重要。 然而，与此同时，不适当的组织结构会扼杀技术进步。 同样重要的是，强大组织的控制者可以选择和培养只为自己利益服务的技术。 这个问题不仅限于商业组织； 它也可以体现在公共部门。 因此，我们将把注意力转向最大和可能最强大的组织：联邦政府。
The last chapter put forth the claim that organizations play a major role in determining the kind of technologies we get. To be sure, these organizations are not all-powerful. When business firms are involved, consumers can affect technological change by deciding whether or not to buy their products. As employees, we might be able to exert some influence through our acceptance or rejection of new workplace technologies. But not all of the major decisions affecting the trajectory of technological change are made in the private sector. To a large extent, government organizations influence technological choices. In a democratic society, this should expand the power of citizens to get the technologies they want. But do they? Does governmental involvement in the development of technology necessarily result in more beneficial technologies? Are democratic ideals realized in the operation of government policies and processes? These are some of the issues that will be addressed in the following survey of the government's role in shaping technological change. 最后一章将说明组织在决定我们获得的技术类型方面发挥着重要作用。可以肯定的是，组织并不是全能的。当商业公司参与进来时，消费者可以通过决定是否购买他们的产品来影响技术变革。作为员工，我们可以通过接受或拒绝新的工作场所技术来施加一些影响。但并非所有影响技术变革轨迹的重大决策都是在私营部门做出的。在很大程度上，政府组织会影响技术选择。在民主社会中，这应该扩大公民获得他们想要的技术的权力。但是真的如此吗？政府参与技术开发是否一定会产生更有益的技术？民主理想是否在政府政策和程序的运作中被践行？这些是下面政府在塑造技术变革中的作用的调查中将要解决的一些问题。
Government Actions and the Shaping of Technology 政府行为与技术塑造
The involvement of the federal government in technological change is as old as the Republic. The United States of America emerged during an era when technological change was beginning to accelerate, and the framers of the Constitution believed that the government should encourage technological advance through the granting of patents and copyrights to those who had produced new things. Accordingly, Article 1, Section 8, of the Constitution stipulates that Congress is to "promote the Progress of Science and Useful Arts by securing for limited Times to Authors and Inventors the Exclusive Rights to their respective Writings and Discoveries." 联邦政府参与技术变革的历史与共和国一样古老。 美利坚合众国出现在技术变革开始加速的时代，宪法的制定者认为政府应该向创造新事物的人授予专利和版权来鼓励技术进步。 因此，《宪法》第 1 条第 8 款规定，国会将"通过确保作者和发明者在有限时间内获得其各自著作和发现的专有权，以促进科学和实用艺术的进步"。
The government's granting of patent rights provides the legal framework for technological advances generated by individuals and private organizations. The government also supports other types of infrastructure that are essential to the creation, development, and use of modern technologies. Since the ultimate basis of technological advance is the growth of knowledge, governments at all levels do much to indirectly sponsor technological advance through their support of education. Federal aid to individual students has supported the education of large numbers of scientists, engineers, and technicians. Moreover, in recent decades, institutions of higher learning have been major sources of technological advance through their research activities. These activities were strongly encouraged by the passage of P.L. 96-517, commonly known as the Bayh-Dole Act, in 1980. Under its provisions, universities receiving federal research funds that aid in the creation of innovative products and processes can obtain patents on them. Although some universities have reaped substantial revenues from these patents, critics have voiced concerns that the pursuit of these revenues has undermined some of the basic values of the university, such as the pursuit of knowledge for its own sake and the free transmission of knowledge. Moreover, the pursuit of patents has not been as lucrative as many have hoped. A few patents have been spectacularly successful from a financial standpoint; the gene-splicing technology developed by Herbert Boyer and Stanley Cohen brought $200 million in revenues to Stanford University and the University of California, San Francisco. But patenting has not produced financial windfalls for most institutions; two-thirds of the revenues generated by university-held patents have gone to only 13 institutions. 政府授予专利权为个人和私人组织创造的技术进步提供了法律框架。 政府还支持对现代技术的创新、发展、运用至关重要的其他类型的基础设施。 由于知识的增长是技术进步的基础，各级政府都做了很多工作，通过对教育的支持来间接支持技术进步。 联邦对个别学生的援助支持了大量科学家、工程师和技术人员的教育。 此外，近几十年来，高等教育机构通过其研究活动成为技术进步的主要来源。这些活动受到了 P.L. 96-517，通常称为 1980 年的 Bayh-Dole 法案的鼓励。根据该法案的规定，接受联邦研究基金以帮助研发创新产品和工艺的大学可以获得相关专利。 尽管一些大学从这些专利中获得了可观的收入，但批评人士表示，对这些收入的追求损害了大学的一些基本价值观，例如为了知识而追求知识和知识的自由传播。此外，对专利的追求并不像许多人希望的那样有利可图。 从财务角度来看，一些专利取得了惊人的成功； Herbert Boyer 和 Stanley Cohen 开发的基因剪接技术为斯坦福大学和加州大学旧金山分校带来了 2 亿美元的收入。 但专利申请并没有为大多数机构带来经济上的意外收获。 大学拥有的专利收入的三分之二流向了区区家 13 个机构。
In addition to maintaining the patent system and supporting education and university research, government programs also provide the auxiliary goods and services that are essential for the use of particular technologies. For example, high-speed air travel requires more than just jet aircraft; equally important are government-supported airports, air traffic controllers, weather forecasts, and safety inspections. To take another obvious example, the effective use of automobiles is dependent on a network of roads and highways, as well as driver training in the schools, the enactment and enforcement of traffic laws, and so on. 除了维持专利制度、支持教育和大学研究外，政府计划还提供使用特定技术必不可少的辅助产品和服务。 例如，高速航空旅行需要的不仅仅是喷气式飞机； 政府投资的机场、空中交通管制员、天气预报和安全检查等同样重要。 再举一个明显的例子，汽车的高效使用取决于道路和高速公路网络，以及学校的驾驶员培训、交通法规的制定和执行等。
The case of the automobile brings up another reason for government involvement in technological matters. Every significant technological change brings with it an assortment of auxiliary consequences, some of them pernicious. The private automobile has generated many benefits, but it has also created a number of problems. These problems are not borne exclusively by individual car owners, and for this reason they are known as "negative externalities." That is, they are costs that are not directly taken into account when a person buys a car and puts it on the road; they are external to the market exchange between the buyer and the seller of the car. In operating a car, the owner incurs a number of personal costs: gas, insurance, repairs, and monthly payments that seem to go on forever. But at the same time, the operation of the car results in costs for the society as a whole: increased pollution, congestion, and so on. Since these costs are not included in the market transaction, governmental action is necessary. To take a notable example, the negative externality of automobile-generated air pollution is commonly addressed by regulations that require the installation of emission-control devices. Alternatively, the government could assess an emission tax, thereby making it financially advantageous for an owner to install these devices. 汽车的案例提出了政府参与技术事务的另一个原因。每一次重大的技术变革都会带来各种各样的连带后果，其中一些是有害的。私家车带来了很多好处，但也带来了一些问题。这些问题并不完全由车主个人承担，因此被称为"负外部性"。也就是说，它们是人们购买汽车并上路时没有直接考虑的成本；它们在汽车的买方和卖方之间的市场交易之外。在驾驶汽车时，车主会产生许多个人费用：汽油、保险、维修和似乎永远持续下去的每月付款。但与此同时，汽车的运行也会给整个社会带来成本：污染加剧、拥堵等等。由于这些成本不包括在市场交易中，因此需要政府采取行动。举一个值得注意的例子，汽车产生的空气污染的负面外部性通常通过要求安装排放控制装置的法规来解决。或者，政府可以评估排放税，从而使所有者安装这些设备在经济上有利。
Some government policies and activities are not aimed directly at technological change, but they can strongly influence its scope and direction nonetheless. Tax policies can affect technological change by encouraging capital investments that often embody new technologies. Capital investment can be stimulated to some degree by taxing the income derived from investments at a lower rate than other sources of income. As a result, individuals and firms are motivated to invest their money in new machines and other productive goods. Capital investment can also be encouraged by allowing the accelerated depreciation of capital equipment. This means that the cost of a machine or other piece of equipment with a useful life of, say, 20 years can be used to offset taxes during a much shorter period. As a result, a firm's immediate profits are increased. Since business executives tend to be primarily concerned with short-term performance, accelerated depreciation can stimulate capital investments that embody new technologies. 一些政府政策和活动并不直接针对技术变革，但它们仍然可以强烈影响变革范围和方向。税收政策可以通过鼓励那些拥有新技术的资本投资来影响技术变革。通过以低于其他收入来源的税率对投资所得征税，可以在一定程度上刺激资本投资。因此，个人和公司有动力将资金投资于新设备和其他生产性产品。允许资本设备加速折旧也可以鼓励资本投资。这意味着一台机器的使用年限为 20 年，其成本可用于抵扣一段更短时间内的税收。这样做的结果是，公司的直接利润增加了。由于企业高管往往首要关注短期业绩，加速折旧可以刺激体现新技术的资本投资。
The government can also encourage the development and use of specific technologies by offering tax credits or deductions to those willing to invest in them. For many years the federal tax code provided an important benefit for oil producers by granting a depletion allowance that was used to offset corporate taxes. One result was the expansion of petroleum-based energy technologies. A different approach was taken during the 1970s when the energy crises of that period generated a strong interest in alternative sources of energy. One governmental response was to offer generous tax credits to people investing in wind-powered electrical generators, and as a result large numbers of wind turbines have been built in some areas. 政府还可以通过向愿意投资特定技术的人提供税收抵免或扣除来鼓励开发和使用特定技术。 多年来，联邦税法通过授予用于抵消公司税的损耗津贴为石油生产商提供了重要的好处。 结果之一是扩展了以石油为基础的能源技术。 在 1970 年代，当时的能源危机引发了人们对替代能源的浓厚兴趣，当时采取了不同的方法。 政府的一项回应是向投资风力发电机的人们提供慷慨的税收抵免，因此在一些地区建造了大量的风力涡轮机。
As we have seen, innovation does not always respect existing social and legal arrangements, and the courts may be called upon to resolve issues generated by technological change. To take one example, until fairly recently biological parenthood was not a problematic concept; every child had a father and mother who jointly contributed to his or her conception. Since 1978, however, it has been possible to use in-vitro fertilization for this purpose. This practice has led to a number of legal conundrums centering on the definition of parenthood. One such issue has arisen as hundreds of men have had their sperm frozen for future artificial insemination because they suffered from a terminal disease, were soldiers about to be deployed to a combat zone, or simply as a precautionary measure. Some of these men did in fact die prior to a successful insemination and birth, giving rise to this question: Were their children entitled to the Social Security benefits that are paid to children whose father has died? In Florida, one man's widow filed for benefits on behalf of twins that had been born after her husband's death. The agency denied her claim, only to have the decision overturned by an appeals court. But in 2012 the United States Supreme Court unanimously overturned the lower court's decision because Florida barred inheritance for posthumously conceived children. But this is not the end of the matter. Although four states bar posthumously conceived children from receiving inheritances, the laws of 13 other states allow it. The remaining states lack specific laws regarding posthumous inheritance. 正如我们所见，创新并不总是尊重现有的社会和法律安排，法院可能会被要求解决技术变革产生的问题。 举一个例子，直到最近，生物学层面的亲生父母身份才不是一个有疑问的概念。 每个孩子都有一个父亲和母亲，他们共同完成了孩子的受孕。 然而，1978 年开始，已经有人进行了人体的体外受精。 这种做法导致了许多围绕父母身份定义的法律难题。 其中之一是，数百名男性或因患有绝症、或即将被部署到战区，或者仅仅是作为一种预防措施，他们的精子被冷冻以备将来进行人工授精。这导致的一个现实是，一些男性在其精子与卵子成功受精和分娩之前就已经死亡。这就引发了一个问题：他们的孩子是否有权获得支付给父亲去世的孩子的社会保障福利？ 在佛罗里达州，一名男子的遗孀为她丈夫去世后出生的双胞胎申请福利。 机构最初拒绝了她的索赔，但在女子上诉法院后它们推翻了该决定。 但在 2012 年，美国最高法院一致推翻了下级法院的裁决，禁止佛罗里达州死后怀孕的孩子继承遗产。 但这并不是事情的结束。 尽管有四个州禁止死后怀孕的孩子继承遗产，但其他 13 个州的法律允许这样做。 而剩下州则缺乏关于死后继承的具体法律。
What is fair and proper in cases such as these? This situation will if anything become more common in the years to come; children can be born decades after the death of their biological father, given that frozen sperm can retain viability for up to 100 years. Issues such as these will become even more prominent in the future as advances in reproductive technologies alter the essential nature of parenthood and family. Judges and legislators will confront many issues and challenges regarding child custody, inheritances, and government benefits. 在这样的情况下，怎样评判才是公平的和适当的？ 如果这种情况在未来几年变得更加普遍，将可能出现以下这种情况： 孩子可以在他们的亲生父亲去世几十年后出生，因为冷冻精子可以保留长达 100 年的活力。 随着生殖技术的进步改变了父母和家庭的基本性质，诸如此类的问题在未来将变得更加突出。 法官和立法者将面临许多有关儿童监护权、遗产继承和政府福利的问题和挑战。
In addition to dealing with the consequences of emerging technologies, the federal government is directly involved in the generation of some of these technologies through its support of research and development. The scope of government involvement in R&D has grown massively in the postwar era. In 1940, the federal government spent only $67 million on the direct support of science and technology, the equivalent of about $1.03 billion today. For the 2010 fiscal year, the federal budget for R&D was about $147.1 billion. 除了应对新兴技术的后果外，联邦政府还通过其对研发的支持直接参与其中一些技术的产生。 战后时期，政府参与研发的范围大幅增加。 1940年，联邦政府在直接支持科学技术上的花费仅为6700万美元，相当于今天的约10.3亿美元。 而到了 2010 财年，联邦研发预算则成长到约 1471 亿美元。
Over the last few decades, government involvement in research has been skewed in favor of defense and space exploration. By the time of the last lunar landing, in late 1972, the Apollo program entailed expenditures of $19.4 billion, about $115 billion in today's dollars. More recently, the cost of the construction of the International Space Station came to about $100 billion dollars over a 12-year period, and its operation absorbs about $1.5 billion annually. In the 1984 fiscal year, a massive peacetime military buildup resulted in military R&D expenditures of $31.8 billion, almost 70 percent of the total federal R&D budget. The waning of the Cold War resulted in a significant reduction in the proportion of R&D funds allocated to defense. Even so, the military R&D budget for the 2010 fiscal year came to more than $82 billion, about 55 percent of the total federal R&D budget.Moreover, since 9/11 the federal government has greatly increased antiterrorism research and development. Support for technologies aimed at foiling terrorist attacks has increased significantly, as has R&D for code breaking. The extent of funding for the latter is classified, but it is known that the National Security Agency, the highly secretive organization that oversees this research, possessed the world's fastest computer in 2009 and is sponsoring the construction of an even faster one today. The raw data for these supercomputers will come from everything from personal e-mails and telephone records to bookstore purchases and travel itineraries, all of it intercepted and aggregated in a complex being built in Utah that will be five times the size of the U.S. Capitol. 在过去的几十年中，政府对研究的参与一直偏向于国防和太空探索。 在1972 年末最后一次登月时，阿波罗计划的支出为 194 亿美元，以今天的美元计算约为 1150 亿美元。 更近一些的案例是，国际空间站的建设成本在 12 年内达到了约 1000 亿美元，其运营每年达到约 15 亿美元。 在 1984 财政年度，和平时期大规模的军事集结导致军事研发支出达到 318 亿美元，几乎占联邦研发预算总额的 70%。冷战的结束导致分配给国防的研发资金比例显着减少。 即便如此，2010 财年的军事研发预算仍超过 820 亿美元，约占联邦研发预算总额的 55%。 此外，自 9/11 以来，联邦政府大大增加了反恐研究和开发。 对旨在挫败恐怖袭击的技术的支持显着增加，密码破解的研发也是如此。后者的资金规模属于机密，但众所周知，负责监督这项研究的高度机密组织国家安全局在 2009 年拥有世界上最快的计算机，并在今天赞助建造速度更快的计算机。 这些超级计算机的原始数据将来自从个人电子邮件和电话记录到书店购买和旅行行程的所有内容，所有这些都在犹他州建造的一个综合体中被拦截和汇总，该综合体将是美国国会大厦的五倍。
Although the military sector absorbs a large portion of federal R&D resources, the funds allocated for other purposes are still considerable. In the 2010 fiscal year the federal budget for civilian R&D was $66.3 billion, with health and human services and energy accounting for $31.2 billion and $10.7 billion, respectively. All in all, by supplying about half of the funds used for the nation's R&D efforts, the federal government plays a very large role in the sponsorship of the nation's R&D. In turn, the allocation of federal R&D funds can significantly influence the direction of technological advance. To take a notable example, from fiscal year 2003 to 2012the federal government spent a total of nearly $40 billion on energy R&D. Of that sum, 25.4 percent went for fossil fuel R&D, and another 25.9 percent went to nuclear R&D, while R&D funds for energy efficiency and renewable energy accounted for 16.4 percent and 17.1 percent, respectively. 虽然军工部门吸收了很大一部分联邦研发资源，但拨给其他用途的资金仍然相当可观。 2010 财年，民用研发的联邦预算为 663 亿美元，其中卫生和人类服务以及能源分别占 312 亿美元和 107 亿美元。 总而言之，通过提供大约一半用于国家研发工作的资金，联邦政府在赞助国家研发方面发挥了非常大的作用。 与此同时，联邦研发资金的分配可以显着影响技术进步的方向。 举一个显着的例子，从 2003 财年到 2012 财年，联邦政府在能源研发上总共花费了近 400 亿美元。 其中，化石燃料研发占25.4%，核能研发占25.9%，能效和可再生能源研发资金分别占16.4%和17.1%。
But Is It Really Necessary? 但这真的有必要吗？
Why has government involvement in technological development increased to such a marked degree in the postwar era? In part it is due to the recognition that our prosperity is tied to our ability to advance technologically. Given the fierce competition of the international economy, the failure to maintain high technological levels can have severe consequences. Japan recognized this fact, and its Ministry of International Trade and Industry (MITI, now METI, the Ministry of Economy, Trade, and Industry) aggressively sponsored the development of selected high-technology industries such as semiconductors, genetic engineering, robots, and composite materials. Not only had it provided research funds, MITI also organized cooperative joint research efforts between firms in the same industry so that they could do collectively what they could not do individually. 为什么政府在战后时代对技术发展的参与增加到如此显着的程度？ 部分原因是人们认识到我们的繁荣与我们的技术进步能力息息相关。 鉴于国际经济的激烈竞争，技术落后会产生严重后果。 日本认识到这一事实，其通商产业省（MITI，现为经济产业省）积极支持半导体、基因工程、机器人和复合材料等选定高科技产业的发展。 不仅提供研究经费，通商产业省还组织同行业企业之间的合作联合研究工作，使他们可以集体做他们不能单独做的事情。
The government of the United States has been less explicit in its sponsorship of technological advance, but it still has played a major role. The development of computers and semiconductors during the early 1950s was extensively supported by federal funds for research and development. Equally important, government procurement of the resulting products created a market at a time when sales within the private sector did not seem promising. In similar fashion, government procurement of aircraft engines and other components provided a strong stimulus for technological advances that spilled over into commercial aviation. Military needs were of course the main source of these efforts. Accordingly, it can be argued that during the postwar era the United States has had a de facto policy of supporting technological development, but unlike Japan, much of it has been driven by military rather than commercial considerations. 美国政府在赞助技术进步方面的作用没有那么明确，但它仍然发挥了重要作用。 1950 年代初期计算机和半导体的发展得到了联邦研发基金的广泛支持。 同样重要的是，在私营部门销售不乐观的时候，政府采购为产品的诞生创造了一个市场。类似地，政府采购飞机发动机和其他部件为技术进步提供了强有力的刺激，这些进步已经延伸到商业航空领域。 军事需求当然是这些努力的主要来源。 因此，可以说，在战后时代，美国实际上有支持技术发展的政策，但与日本不同的是，其中大部分是出于军事而非商业考虑。
Important though they are, military requirements are not the sole justification for government support of technological advance. Although the market system has served as midwife to an abundance of innovative technologies, it cannot be expected to stimulate every type of technological innovation. Certain kinds of technological advances have little appeal to individual entrepreneurs, for they cannot be "packaged" for sale to individual consumers. Moreover, once these technologies are in place, they presumably benefit everyone, whether they pay for them or not. This is the so-called free rider problem. For example, some people may be ardent supporters of a cleaner environment, but if they were to individually pay for a power plant's smokestack scrubbers, everyone in the community would benefit equally, even though most of them made no financial contributions to the installation of the scrubbers. Under these circumstances, the government has to take the lead by mandating the development and installation of emission-control equipment or assessing a pollution tax that stimulates their installation. The costs would be borne by the operators of the power plant, who would likely pass them along to consumers in the form of higher utility bills. Alternatively, the government could subsidize the installation of scrubbers, and offset the subsidy by levying a tax. 尽管很重要，但军事要求并不是政府支持技术进步的唯一理由。 虽然市场体系已经成为了大量创新技术的助产士，但不能指望它刺激每一种技术创新。 某些类型的技术进步对个体企业家几乎没有吸引力，因为它们不能被"包装"出售给个体消费者。 此外，一旦这些技术到位，无论他们是否付费，它们都可能使所有人受益。 这就是所谓的搭便车问题。例如，有些人可能是环境保护的热心支持者，但如果他们要为发电厂的烟囱洗涤器单独付费，社区中的每个人都将平等受益，即使他们中的大多数人没有为安装洗涤器提供任何资金。在这种情况下，政府必须带头强制开发和安装排放控制设备，或评估刺激安装的污染税。 成本将由发电厂的运营商承担，他们可能会以更高的水电费的形式转嫁给消费者。 或者，政府可以补贴洗涤器的安装并通过征税来抵消补贴。
Some activities produce benefits that are considerably greater than the returns that accrue to the individuals or firms that engage in them In contrast to negative externalities, these can be labeled "positive externalities." In some cases, the potential social benefits may be great, but the private rate of return may be so small that no private party is willing to undertake them. This is frequently the case with basic research that has no direct payoff but provides a foundation for subsequent technological applications. Moreover, once the research has been done, the knowledge gained can be made available to everyone at little additional cost, thereby increasing its benefits to society as a whole. Under these circumstances it makes sense for the government to sponsor basic research, paying for it through taxation. This is precisely what has happened: 57 percent of the "pure" scientific research conducted in the United States is financed by the federal government and an additional 26 percent is funded by universities and other nonprofit agencies. 一些活动产生的收益远远大于从事这些活动的个人或公司所获得的回报。与负外部性相反，这些活动可以被称为"正外部性"。 在某些情况下，潜在的社会效益可能很大，但私人回报率可能太小，以至于没有私人方愿意承担。 没有直接回报但为后续技术应用提供基础的基础研究通常就是这种情况。此外，一旦研究完成，所获得的知识就可以以很少的额外成本提供给每个人，从而增加其对整个社会的好处。 在这种情况下，政府资助基础研究并通过税收来支付是有意义的。 这正是发生的事情：在美国进行的"纯"科学研究中有 57% 由联邦政府资助，另外 26% 由大学和其他非营利机构资助。
Government Institutions for the Guidance of Technology 政府技术指导机构
A modern nation's economic and military security is closely tied to its ability to generate and absorb new technologies. At the same time, simply coping with all of the consequences of technological change can require the leadership and organization that only government can provide. For these reasons, many governments have established special departments and ministries charged with the promotion, control, and governance of technology. But this has not been the case in the United States. There is no cabinet-level Department of Technology, only a collection of congressional committees and government agencies that involve themselves in a plethora of separate issues and decisions. Some of these agencies reside within the executive branch as parts of cabinet-level departments (such as the Department of Energy's Nuclear Regulatory Commission), while others (such as NASA and the National Science Foundation) are quasi-independent agencies directly under the president. 现代国家的经济和军事安全与其产生和吸收新技术的能力密切相关。 与此同时，简单地应对技术变革的所有后果可能需要只有政府才能提供的领导和组织。 由于这些原因，许多政府设立了专门的部门和部委，负责技术的推广、控制和治理。 但在美国，情况并非如此。 没有内阁级的技术部，只有一组国会委员会和政府机构，它们参与了大量不同的问题和决定。 其中一些机构作为内阁级部门（如能源部核管理委员会）的一部分驻留在行政部门内，而其他机构（如 NASA 和国家科学基金会）则是直接在总统领导下的准独立机构。
The executive branch is best situated to bring some degree of coherence to technology policy, and in fact the president and his staff have on occasion played significant roles in determining the course of a particular technology by influencing legislation, designating agency heads, impounding funds, and using the other tools available to the president. The importance of having the president well advised on scientific and technological matters was recognized in 1957 with the formation of the Presidential Science Advisory Committee (PSAC) within the Eisenhower administration. PSAC was largely concerned with matters relating to defense and space, and when its members failed to support President Nixon's policies on missile defense and the construction of a supersonic airliner, PSAC was abolished in 1973 and some of its functions were transferred to the National Science Foundation. A formal structure for providing scientific and technical advice for the president was reconstituted in 1976 with the formation of the Office of Science and Technology Policy (OSTP). The director of OSTP also serves as a member of the National Science and Technology Council, which was established by a 1993 executive order of President Clinton. In addition to the OSTP director, the council includes the president, vice president, and several cabinet-level officials and high-level administrators. Among its responsibilities are coordinating the science and technology policy-making process, making science and technology policies and programs consistent with the goals of the administration, and furthering international cooperation in science and technology. It is also the domain of the Chief Technology Officer, a position created by President Obama in 2009 and whose efforts have been directed toward making the government more effective and accessible through the use of current technologies. 行政部门最适合为技术政策带来一定程度的连贯性，并且事实上，总统和他的工作人员有时通过影响立法、指定机构负责人、扣押资金以及使用总统可用的其他工具，在确定特定技术的进程方面发挥了重要作用。1957 年，随着艾森豪威尔政府内总统科学咨询委员会 (PSAC) 的成立，让总统在科学和技术问题上得到充分建议的重要性得到了认可。 PSAC 主要关注与国防和太空有关的事务，当其成员未能支持尼克松总统的导弹防御政策和建造超音速客机时，PSAC 于 1973 年被废除，其部分职能转移到美国国家科学基金会 .1976 年，随着科学技术政策办公室 (OSTP) 的成立，为总统提供科学和技术建议的正式结构得到了重组。 OSTP 的主任还是国家科学技术委员会的成员，该委员会是根据 1993 年克林顿总统的行政命令成立的。 除了OSTP主任外，该委员会还包括总统、副总统和几位内阁级官员和高级管理人员。 其职责包括协调科技决策过程，使科技政策和计划与政府的目标保持一致，以及促进国际科技合作。 它也是首席技术官的领域，该职位由奥巴马总统于 2009 年设立，其努力旨在通过使用当前技术提高政府的效率和可及性。
Some presidents have had more interest in science and technology policies than others, but direct presidential involvement in the shaping of these policies has been infrequent in all administrations. On a few occasions, however, it has been highly significant. President Reagan's Strategic Defense Initiative (the "Star Wars" ballistic missile defense system) represented a major redirection of American defense policy, yet it began as an idiosyncratic effort. The president publicly announced the program only five days after informing his science adviser, while the joint chiefs of staff, the secretary of state, and the secretary of defense got only two days' notice. The chief scientist for the Pentagon learned of the proposal only nine hours before the speech that presented the program to the nation. 一些总统比其他总统对科技政策更感兴趣，但总统直接参与这些政策的制定在所有政府中都很少见。 然而，在某些情况下，它非常重要。 里根总统的战略防御计划（"星球大战"弹道导弹防御系统）代表了美国国防政策的重大转变，但它开始时是一种特殊的努力。 总统在通知他的科学顾问后仅五天就公开宣布了该计划，而参谋长联席会议、国务卿和国防部长仅提前两天收到通知。 五角大楼的首席科学家在向全国展示该计划的演讲前九个小时才得知该计划。
With presidential involvement in the setting of technology policy largely confined to a few major policy decisions, the day-to-day shaping of technological policy tends to be the business of Congress and various government agencies. Here, the disjointed nature of American technology policy is apparent. There is no unified approach to the budgeting of funds for research and development: over a dozen appropriation subcommittees in each house of Congress take a hand in determining the budgets of the agencies they oversee. These committees and subcommittees often have to address issues directly connected to technological matters. Congressional involvement with technological issues was recognized in 1972 by the creation of the Office of Technology Assessment (OTA), which had as its purpose the provision of information to Congress to help guide its decisions about technological policy, and to give it more leverage over the president in science and technology matters. OTA investigated a wide selection of topics that ranged from an examination of the physiological basis of drug addiction to an evaluation of the Social Security Administration's plans to upgrade its computer facilities. In its early years OTA was criticized for not taking on highly controversial topics, but it eventually became involved in contentious matters like the effectiveness of a proposed antimissile defense system. In the latter case, the publication of its report was delayed by a lengthy classification review, and in the end several key chapters were deleted due to the objections of the Defense Department. It is likely that the Defense Department's opposition had more to do with the negative tone of the report than with concerns about its revelation of military secrets. 由于总统对技术政策制定的参与主要限于少数重大政策决定，因此技术政策的日常制定往往是国会和各种政府机构的事务。 在这里，美国技术政策的脱节性质显而易见。 研究和开发资金的预算没有统一的方法：国会两院的十多个拨款小组委员会参与确定他们监督机构的预算。 这些委员会和小组委员会通常不得不处理与技术问题直接相关的问题。1972 年，技术评估办公室 (OTA) 的成立承认了国会对技术问题的参与，其目的是向国会提供信息，以帮助指导其有关技术政策的决策，并在科学和技术问题上赋予其对总统更多的影响力。OTA 调查了广泛的主题，从对毒瘾的生理基础的检查到对社会保障管理局升级其计算机设施的计划的评估。 早年，OTA 因没有处理极具争议的话题而受到批评，但它最终卷入了一些有争议的问题，例如拟议的反导弹防御系统的有效性。 在后一种情况下，其报告的发布因冗长的分类审查而被推迟，最终因国防部的反对而删除了几个关键章节。 国防部的反对可能更多地与报告的负面基调有关，而不是担心其泄露军事机密。
As the last example indicates, OTA sometimes found it difficult to achieve a balance between the goals of its overseers in the federal government and the objectivity and neutrality characteristic of scholarly inquiry. Given the contentiousness of many technological issues and the frequent difficulty of separating facts from values, OTA was in an inherently precarious situation. Being on the "wrong side" in some controversial issues undercut OTA's support in Congress, especially after Republicans gained control of both houses in 1994. Despite strong bipartisan agreement on the value of OTA outside Congress, the office was dismantled a year later. Its demise seems to confirm the old joke that powerful individuals and groups tend to use expertise the way that a drunk uses a lamppost—more for support than for illumination. 正如最后一个例子所表明的，OTA 有时发现很难在联邦政府监督者的目标与学术调查的客观性和中立性特征之间取得平衡。 鉴于许多技术问题的争议性以及经常难以将事实与价值区分开来，OTA 处于一种内在的不稳定状态。 在一些有争议的问题上站在"错误的一边"削弱了 OTA 在国会的支持，特别是在 1994 年共和党获得两院的控制权之后。 尽管两党在国会之外就 OTA 的价值达成了强烈的共识，但该办公室在一年后被拆除。 它的消亡似乎证实了一个古老的笑话，即有权势的个人和团体倾向于像醉汉使用灯柱一样使用专业知识——更多是为了支持而不是照明。
As far as the actual working of Congress is concerned, policies relating to technology emerge from the many committees and subcommittees of the two legislative branches. Legislation affecting the development and use of technology is forged in bodies as disparate in their concerns as the House Armed Services Subcommittee and the Senate Agriculture Committee. These committees and subcommittees often work in conjunction with federal agencies and departments, such as NASA or the Department of Defense, that administer a particular technological sector. 就国会的实际工作而言，与技术相关的政策来自两个立法部门的许多委员会和小组委员会。 影响技术开发和使用的立法是在与众议院军事小组委员会和参议院农业委员会等不同的机构中制定的。 这些委员会和小组委员会通常与管理特定技术部门的联邦机构和部门合作，例如 NASA 或国防部。
Processes 流程
The most direct way that Congress determines the course of technological development is through passing laws that either forbid the use of a particular technology or regulate the way it is used. Indeed, the very notion that the government has a legitimate right to regulate private industry originated with the need to address a problem presented by a new technology—the explosion of riverboat steam boilers in the first half of the nineteenth century. The Franklin Institute in Philadelphia was given the task of investigating the construction and operation of boilers. Its report provided a wealth of information about boilers and their components, as well as a set of recommendations regarding their operation and maintenance, many of which were subsequently written into law by Congress. Today, government regulations cover a vast number of technological concerns, everything from the siting of nuclear power plants to the length of trucks. 国会决定技术发展进程的最直接方式是通过法律，禁止使用特定技术或规范使用方式。 事实上，政府有合法权利监管私营工业的想法源于解决新技术所带来的问题——19 世纪上半叶河船蒸汽锅炉的爆炸式增长。 费城富兰克林研究所的任务是调查锅炉的建造和运行。 其报告提供了有关锅炉及其组件的大量信息，以及一系列有关其操作和维护的建议，其中许多建议随后被国会写入法律。 今天，政府法规涵盖了大量的技术问题，从核电厂的选址到卡车的长度，无所不包。
Along with the passage of laws and regulations, the federal government affects the course of technological development through the budgetary process; that is, by deciding to pay for certain kinds of technologies and not others. In some cases, government financial support can be crucial. The supersonic transport plane (SST) literally never got off the ground because in 1971 Congress voted not to appropriate any more funds for its development. Also, as we have seen in Chapter 8, the George W. Bush administration severely restricted stem-cell research that used human embryos. Conversely, some technologies, such as civilian nuclear power, have received a large amount of financial and legal support from the federal government that has been crucial to their development and use. 随着法律法规的通过，联邦政府通过预算程序影响技术发展的进程； 也就是说，通过决定为某些类型的技术而不是其他技术付费。 在某些情况下，政府的财政支持可能是至关重要的。 超音速运输机 (SST) 实际上从未起飞，因为 1971 年国会投票决定不再为其开发拨款。 此外，正如我们在第 8 章中看到的，乔治·W·布什政府严格限制使用人类胚胎的干细胞研究。 相反，一些技术，如民用核电，得到了联邦政府的大量财政和法律支持，这对其开发和使用至关重要。
Governmental decisions that affect technological development do not take place in a political vacuum. It often happens that technologies are sponsored because they have substantial outside support. Gaining government interest in addressing a technological issue is a crucial first step, and one that cannot be taken for granted. Here again, the piecemeal approach to governing technological change is evident. There is no clear and comprehensive approach to deciding what technological goals should (and should not) be pursued so that a governmental agenda can be set. Instead of being the product of calm deliberation, an issue is often put on the agenda because of some "focusing event"; an oil embargo forces a consideration of the energy technologies we use; the launch of Sputnik by the Soviet Union demonstrates the apparent need for an accelerated U.S. space program; a serious accident reveals material and organizational defects in the operation of nuclear power plants. 影响技术发展的政府决策不是在政治真空中进行的。 通常情况下，技术得到赞助是因为它们有大量的外部支持。 让政府对特定问题感兴趣是至关重要的第一步，而且不能想当然认为政府会同意。 在这里，管理技术变革的零散手段再次显而易见。 没有明确和全面的方法来决定应该（和不应该）追求哪些技术目标，用来制定政府议程。 一个问题往往不是冷静思考的产物，而是被一些"焦点事件"掌控议程； 石油禁运迫使人们考虑我们使用的能源技术； 苏联发射人造卫星表明美国显然需要加速太空计划； 一次严重事故揭示了核电厂运行中的物质和组织缺陷。
A sense of crisis and the need for decisive action also emerge when a social movement is directed at a particular technology. Some social movements have taken on well-established technologies that had remained under the radar until they became the subject of media exposés, notably hydraulic fracturing, or "fracking," for the extraction of oil and gas. But large-scale protests are more likely to emerge when a new technological possibility lies just over the horizon. Technologies that have already been established, whatever their unfortunate consequences, simply do not generate the kind of concerns that new ones do. Cars, along with giving us our prized freedom of mobility, also befoul our environment, encourage ugly sprawl, and in 2010 killed nearly 33,000 people in the United States, the equivalent of a major commercial airline crash every two days. Yet few people consider bringing them under tighter governmental regulation or even abolishing them altogether. 当社会运动针对特定技术时，也会出现危机感和采取果断行动的需要。 一些社会运动已经采用了成熟的技术，这些技术在成为媒体曝光的主题之前一直未被关注，特别是用于开采石油和天然气的水力压裂或"压裂"。 但是，当新技术的可能性即将出现时，更有可能出现大规模抗议。 已经建立的技术，无论其带来的不幸后果如何，都不会像新的技术那样产生担忧。 汽车给我们带来了宝贵的行动自由，同时也污染了我们的环境，助长了丑陋的蔓延，2010 年在美国造成近 33,000 人死亡，这相当于每两天发生一次大型商业航空公司坠毁事故。 然而，很少有人考虑将它们置于更严格的政府监管之下，甚至完全废除它们。
Only a few technologies have generated much popular opposition. Such diverse technologies as the chlorination of water, the extensive use of medical X-rays, microwave ovens, and birth-control pills have received, at best, passing attention, and no sustained effort to subject them to governmental control. In fact, it is not entirely clear why some technologies and not others become the focus of widespread concern. But it is certainly true that a technology that produces large-scale failures, such as a nuclear reactor accident, is more likely to evince opposition than one that produces a series of small-scale failures, even though in aggregate their consequences may be great, as has been the case with automobiles. And it is also the case that media exposure can greatly heighten opposition to a technology with evident problems. Again, this sort of exposure is more likely when the failure is large and spectacular rather than diffuse and important only in the aggregate. 只有少数技术引起了广泛的反对。 诸如氯化水、广泛使用医用 X 射线、微波炉和避孕药等多种多样的技术，对这些技术充其量只是一时的关注，并且没有持续性的努力使它们受到政府的监管。 事实上，为什么某些技术而不是另一些成为广泛关注的焦点，目前尚不完全清楚。 但确实，一项导致大型事故（例如核反应堆事故）的技术比产生一系列小规模故障的技术更容易遭到反对，尽管总的来说，它们的后果可能很大， 就像汽车的例子一样。 并且媒体曝光也可以极大地加剧对存在明显问题的技术的反对。 同样，当事故后果巨大且集中而不是分散在每个个体上时，这种暴露更有可能发生。
Examples of widespread public debate over new technologies are infrequent; most innovations emerge with little public attention. But this does not mean that politics has been irrelevant. As noted earlier, many new technologies owe their development and diffusion to sponsorship by particular governmental agencies. Since there is no centralized approach to the governance of technology, many key decisions are made at the middle levels of government, that is, by government agencies and congressional committees. It is here that decisions are made to sponsor a particular technology and to create the conditions necessary for its success. Technology policy is the sum of many separate policy actions undertaken at this level. Under these circumstances, the ambitions of individual governmental agencies and their administrators can determine the course of technological development, for an agency has a strong interest in pushing technologies that are in accordance with its own goals, and having them adopted as national policy.This is often achieved with little fanfare. Most decisions about technological policy do not generate much political heat, and a government agency may successfully promote a particular technology with little or no public discussion or debate. 关于新技术的广泛公开辩论的例子并不常见； 大多数创新的出现几乎没有受到公众的关注。 但这并不意味着政治无关紧要。 如前所述，许多新技术的发展和传播归功于特定政府机构的赞助。 由于没有集中管理技术的方法，许多关键决策是在政府中层，即政府机构和国会委员会做出的。 正是在这里做出赞助特定技术并为其成功创造必要条件的决定。技术政策是在这一层面采取的许多独立政策行动的总和。 在这种情况下，各个政府机构及其管理者的野心可以决定技术发展的进程，因为一个机构对推动符合自身目标的技术并将其作为国家政策采用具有浓厚的兴趣。 这通常是在不张扬的情况下实现的。 大多数关于技术政策的决定不会产生太多的政治热度，政府机构可能会成功地推广一项特定的技术，而很少或根本没有公开讨论或辩论。
The importance of government sponsorship can be seen in the history ofatomic power in the United States. In the mid-1950s, the electrical utilities, the greatest potential users of nuclear power, had little reason to make use of the new technology. According to one utility company president, "We weren't anxious to get into nuclear power, and I don't think any other company in its right mind wanted to get into it either." To overcome this reticence, the key government agency, the Atomic Energy Commission, engaged in a large-scale selling job. A demonstration plant was built at Shippingport, Pennsylvania, in 1954, and technical assistance was offered to the industry, along with subsidized prices for nuclear fuel. This is not to say that the Atomic Energy Commission's actions were illegitimate or that civilian nuclear power owes its existence solely to government support, but it does show how national policy can be shaped by the interests of a particular government agency. 政府资助的重要性可见于美国的原子能发展史。 在 1950 年代中期，作为核能最大潜在用户的电力公司几乎没有理由利用这项新技术。 一位公用事业公司总裁表示，"我们并不急于进入核电领域，我认为其他任何心智正常的公司也不想进入核电领域。" 为了克服这种沉默，主要的政府机构原子能委员会进行了大规模的销售工作。 1954 年在宾夕法尼亚州希普林波特建造了一座示范工厂，并为该行业提供了技术援助以及核燃料的补贴价格。 这并不是说原子能委员会的行为是非法的，或者民用核能的存在完全归功于政府的支持，但它确实表明国家政策可以如何受到特定政府机构的利益的影响。
Since some government agencies are more powerful than others, their programs forge ahead while other agencies' projects languish. As a result, potentially significant programs are not enacted, or if enacted they are chronically underfunded, while more dubious ones move ahead. A few agencies are more influential than others because of the greater technical abilities of their staff and their greater interest in science and technology. But in many cases what really matters is who their clients are. Government agencies do not operate in splendid isolation; they are often closely tied to a particular set of clients. As we have seen with the Federal Communications Commission in Chapter 13, even when the task of the agency is regulation, it may be "captured" by the industry that it is supposed to regulate. This happens because the agency needs the support of the industry it oversees in order to maintain its legitimacy and resources. An agency may even delegate to the industry some of the regulatory tasks that it is charged with performing. For example, much of the inspection work performed before the Federal Aviation Administration certifies the airworthiness of a new airplane is actually done by engineers and technicians in the employ of the plane's manufacturer. 由于一些政府机构比其他机构更强大，他们的项目往往拥有更高的优先级。 结果是，一些可能的重要计划没有颁布，或者即使颁布了，它们也会长期资金不足，而更多可疑的项目则继续推进。 少数机构比其他机构更有影响力，因为其员工的技术能力更强，并且对科学和技术更感兴趣。 但是在很多情况下，真正重要的是他们的客户是谁。 政府机构并非孤立地运作； 它们通常与一组特定的客户紧密相关。正如我们在第 13 章中与联邦通信委员会所见，即使该机构的任务是监管，它也可能被它应该监管的行业"捕获"。 之所以发生这种情况，是因为该机构需要其监管的行业的支持，以维持其合法性和资源。 一个机构甚至可以将它负责执行的一些监管任务委托给行业。 例如，在美国联邦航空管理局认证新飞机适航之前进行的大部分检查工作实际上是由受雇于飞机制造商的工程师和技术人员完成的。
The close involvement of government agencies with powerful clients often results in the support of technologies that favor these clients. A great deal of government-sponsored agricultural research has focused on productivity improvements that require mechanization and generally high capital investments. Such research has benefited large, wealthy farmers most of all, and it has even contributed to the decline of small farms and the displacement of rural labor. But large farmers provide the bedrock of political support for the Department of Agriculture, and as a result this agency has primarily sponsored technological developments that benefit its most important and powerful clientele. It has been argued that government-sponsored technological development in general has been strongly oriented to the support of centralized, capital-intensive industries; the result, according to some critics, has been unemployment, environmental damage, increased energy consumption, and greater economic concentration. 政府机构与强大客户的密切参与往往会导致支持这些客户的技术。 大量政府资助的农业研究都集中在需要机械化和高资本投资的生产力提高上。 此类研究最让富裕的大农场主受益，甚至导致小农场的衰落和农村劳动力的转移。但大农场主是农业部政治支持的基本盘，因此，该机构主要赞助技术发展，使其最重要和最强大的客户受益。 有人认为，一般来说，政府资助的技术发展强烈倾向于支持集中的资本密集型产业； 一些批评者认为，这样做会带来失业、环境破坏、能源消耗增加和经济集中度提高。
If an industry has a strong interest in a particular technology, it may exert a great deal of influence, so Congress and the relevant government agencies will lend their support to that technology. In turn, members of Congress may find a particular technology to be politically attractive because it offers "pork barrel" benefits to their constituents. Some technologies, especially those in the military sector, have forged ahead because a project has contractors and subcontractors in a large number of congressional districts. Members of Congress quite naturally are likely to support programs that provide jobs and other economic benefits for their states and districts, and are willing to support projects that benefit the constituents of other representatives in return for support of projects that benefit their own. 如果一个行业对某项技术有浓厚的兴趣，这些关注可能会产生很大的影响力，因此国会和相关政府机构会对该技术给予支持。 反过来，国会议员可能会因为某项技术帮助他们"贿赂选民"，而发现它在政治上的吸引力。 对于一些技术，特别是军事领域的技术，可能因为其项目在诸多国会选区有承包商和分包商，而获得支持。 国会议员很自然地倾向于支持为其州和地区提供就业和其他经济利益的计划，并愿意支持有利于其他代表选民的项目，以换取对有利于他们自己的项目的支持。
In sum, as with many other government policies, the direction of technological policy often results from the interaction of an "iron triangle" of congressional committees, government agencies, and the key groups whose interests are closely affected by governmental decisions. The decision to sponsor a new technology, along with the shape that it takes as it is developed, is often determined by these triangles. This means that the government usually doesn't sponsor the development of new technologies as part of a general effort to find solutions to public problems. Rather, a technology is sponsored because a coalition can be formed from the members of the triangle, who see to it that the selected technologies develop in accordance with their own needs and interests. 总之，与许多其他政府政策一样，技术政策的方向往往是国会委员会、政府机构和利益受政府决策密切影响的关键群体之间"铁三角"相互作用的结果。 赞助一项新技术的决定，以及它在开发过程中的状态，通常由这三方决定。 这意味着政府通常不会赞助新技术的开发，作为寻找公共问题解决方案的总体努力的一部分。 相反，支持一项技术是因为可以由三方成员组成联盟，他们负责确保选定的技术根据自己的需求和兴趣发展。
It also happens that once under way, the development of a new technology builds up momentum. The personnel and agencies charged with its development have a strong interest in its continuation, as do potential users. As a result, a technological policy gets locked in place and options are closed off. In the absence of outside pressures, projects are destined to move ahead. Even when a technology has manifest problems of considerable magnitude, the sponsors of the technology will tend to "throw good money after bad," for once the commitment has been made and the program is underway, it often is far more difficult to terminate a program than to continue with it. 此外，一旦开始，新技术的发展就会形成势头。 负责其开发的人员和机构及其潜在用户对其继续发展会抱有浓厚的兴趣。 其结果是，技术政策将难以更改及取消。 在没有外界压力的情况下，项目注定要继续推进。 即使一项技术出现了相当严重的问题，该技术的发起人也往往会"孤注一掷"，因为一旦做出承诺并且项目正在进行中，终止项目往往比继续下去困难得多。
This is one of the greatest defects of our system of governing technology. Technological change is an uncertain process, with many unforeseeable consequences. Efforts to forecast the precise consequences of a new technology so that policies can be constructed in advance to deal with them are doomed to failure. The best that can be hoped is that technologies can be stopped or modified if this should prove necessary. This is easier said than done. The effective governance of technology is faced with a fundamental paradox: change is easiest at the beginning, but this is when the need for it cannot be foreseen. As Ernest Fitzgerald, the whistle-blower we briefly met in Chapter 18, has said of military projects, "There are only two phases to a major program. The first phase: 'It's too early to tell.' The second phase: 'It's too late to stop.' " 这是我们管理技术系统的最大缺陷之一。 技术变革是一个不确定的过程，会产生许多不可预见的后果。 预测新技术的精确后果以便提前制定政策来应对这些后果的努力注定会失败。 可以希望的最好的事情是，如果证明有必要，可以停止或修改技术。 这说起来容易做起来难。 技术的有效治理面临着一个基本的悖论：变革在开始时是最容易的，但此时却无法预见对变革的需求。 正如我们在第 18 章中短暂见过的告密者欧内斯特·菲茨杰拉德 (Ernest Fitzgerald) 在谈到军事项目时所说的那样："一个重大计划只有两个阶段。 第一阶段：'现在说还为时过早。' 第二阶段：'现在停止已经太晚了。'"
In this way, technology appears to be out of control, as many technologies seem to be driven by their own momentum. But this is not really what is happening; seemingly out-of-control technologies move ahead because they suit the real interests of individuals and organizations. Were these to be taken away, there would be far less reason to continue with the development or deployment of the technology. Technologies do not simply stand or fall on their own merits; their success or failure can often be attributed to the political support that they receive. And this political support will likely be a reflection of the distribution of power both inside and outside the corridors of government. Under these circumstances, is there any hope that an unorganized citizenry can have any influence over the way technology develops? It is to this, our last topic, that we will next turn. 这样一来，技术似乎就失控了，因为许多技术似乎是由自己的动力驱动的。 但这并不是真正正在发生的事情。 看似失控的技术之所以能够取得进步，是因为它们符合个人和组织的真正利益。 如果这些前提不复存在，那么继续开发或建设该技术的理由就会少得多。 技术不是简单地根据其自身的优点而定。 他们的成功或失败往往可以归因于他们获得的政治支持。 这种政治支持很可能反映了政府走廊内外的权力分配。 在这种情况下，一个无组织的公民是否有希望对技术的发展方式产生影响？ 这就是我们的最后一个话题，我们马上就会提到。
The Democratic Control of Technology 对技术的民主控制
The decisions and activities of experts, enterprise managers, and government officials have powerfully affected the kinds of technologies that have been developed, where they have been applied, and how their costs have been met. Most of us have been little more than the consumers of technologies that have been developed by people and organizations largely unknown to us. This process has produced spectacular successes and spectacular problems. Technology has extended our lives, lightened some of our burdens, increased our wealth, and kept us amused. At the same time, the advance of technology has left us with some very unpleasant by-products. This is not the place to attempt to determine if the good has outweighed the bad, for so much depends on what we value. Which way of living is preferable: that of the !Kung San, with its relaxed work patterns but material impoverishment and limited control of the environment, or our own, with its abundance of goods and knowledge, but frantic work schedules? In any event, for most of us the choice is moot; unless we decide to become nomadic hunter-gatherers or subsistence farmers, our lives will be lived in a world shaped by modern technology. At issue is not the acceptance or rejection of technology; what matters is how much individual influence we have over the choice of technologies that we use now and will use in the future. 专家、企业管理者和政府官员的决策和活动对已开发的技术种类、应用领域以及成本的支付方式产生了强大的影响。 我们中的大多数人只不过是技术的消费者，而这些技术是由很大程度上不为大众熟知的人和组织开发的。 这个过程产生了巨大的成功和巨大的问题。 科技延长了我们的生活，减轻了我们的一些负担，增加了我们的财富，让我们感到开心。 同时，技术的进步也给我们留下了一些非常不愉快的副产品。这不是试图确定好是否超过坏的地方，因为在很大程度上取决于我们的价值。 哪种生活方式更可取：是如非洲的!困桑人那样拥有轻松的工作，物质相对匮乏，且对环境的控制有限的模式，还是我们自己的，拥有丰富的商品和知识，但工作时间紧张的模式？ 无论如何，对我们大多数人来说，选择是没有意义的。 除非我们决定成为游牧狩猎采集者或自给农民，否则我们的生活将生活在一个由现代技术塑造的世界中。 问题不是接受或拒绝技术； 重要的是我们对我们现在使用和未来将使用的技术的选择有多大的个人影响。
As individuals, are we doomed to the passive acceptance of technological changes that have been decreed by others? Even if technological development has produced more good than bad, it has proceeded in a fashion that has put it beyond our individual control. It seems as though we have struck a bargain whereby we consume the fruits of technological advance in return for delegating to others the power to determine the technologies that shape the basic contours of our lives—everything from what we eat, to how we work, to the way we are entertained. 作为个人，我们是否注定要被动地接受他人所决定的技术变革？ 即使技术发展产生的好处多于坏处，但它的发展方式已经超出了我们个人的控制范围。似乎我们达成了一项交易，我们消耗技术进步的成果，以换取将决定塑造我们生活基本轮廓的技术的权力委托给他人——从我们吃的东西到我们的工作方式，再到我们的娱乐方式。
Most people seem to believe that this is a fair bargain. As we have seen in the first chapter of this book, there is not a great deal of anguish about our reliance on modern technology. Then, too, it must be remembered that democratic participation has its costs. Above all, the expansion of the number of people engaging in technological decision-making can disrupt the orderly processes favored by managers, engineers, and bureaucrats. This follows from the simple arithmetic of participation; the more parties there are to a decision, the harder it is to decide. The result is often a stalemate—"my vote cancels yours." Everybody ends up with veto power, but no one is able to act in a positive fashion. At best, the result is compromise, which may be a reasonable conclusion in some areas, but in matters that require decisive action, such as stopping the spread of weapons of mass destruction or significantly mitigating global warming, a compromise decision may be worthless or even dangerous. 大多数人似乎认为这是一个公平的交易。 正如我们在本书第一章中看到的那样，我们对现代技术的依赖并没有太多的痛苦。 此外，还必须记住，民主参与是有代价的。 最重要的是，参与技术决策的人数的增加可能会破坏经理、工程师和官僚们所青睐的有序流程。 这是从简单的参与算术得出的； 参与决策的当事人越多，就越难做出决定。结果往往是僵持不下——"我的投票取消了你的投票。" 每个人最终都拥有否决权，但没有人能够以积极的方式采取行动。最好的结果是妥协，在某些领域可能是一个合理的结论，但在需要果断行动的问题上，例如阻止大规模杀伤性武器的扩散或显着减缓全球变暖，妥协的决定可能毫无价值，甚至是危险的。
Does this mean that there is no middle ground between an apathetic acceptance of technological change decreed by others and a paralyzing stalemate? Can democratic participation be reconciled with technological advance? Before these questions can be answered, it is obviously necessary to have some workable definition of democracy. A vast amount of thinking and writing has gone into this issue, and we cannot presume to break any new ground here. But most of us could agree that a democratic process is one in which the people as a whole are able to participate in making meaningful choices about the things that affect their lives. The capitalist economic system does contain some democratic elements, for consumers can choose to buy or not buy particular products, and in so doing they affect the course of technological change. There has been a "democratic" affirmation of hybrid cars, but not of battery-powered ones. And certainly consumer choice has dictated the shift to smaller cars whenever gasoline prices shoot up. But these are choices made after the fact. Consumers can choose only between existing alternatives; they cannot determine which alternatives will be made available to them. This is a bit like voting in a referendum; the electorate can decide an issue, but it does not determine which issues are put on the ballot in the first place. 这是否意味着在冷漠接受他人缔造的技术变革与陷入抵抗的僵局之间没有中间立场？ 民主参与可以与技术进步相协调吗？ 在回答这些问题之前，显然有必要对民主进行一些可行的定义。 在这个问题上已经有大量的思考和著作，我们并没有在这里对其有任何新的诠释。 我们大多数人都同意，民主进程是一个全体人民能够参与对影响他们生活的事情做出有意义的选择的进程。资本主义经济体系确实包含一些民主因素，消费者可以选择购买或不购买特定产品，从而影响技术变革的进程。 混合动力汽车得到了"民主"的肯定，但电池驱动的汽车却没有。 当然，每当汽油价格上涨时，消费者的选择就决定了转向小型汽车。 但这些都是事后做出的选择。 消费者只能在现有的替代品之间进行选择； 他们无法确定将提供哪些替代品。 这有点像在全民公决中投票； 选民可以决定一个问题，但他们并不能决定将哪些问题放在选票上。
In similar fashion, democratic choice can be exercised by voting for or against candidates because of their stance on a key technological issue. There have been local elections that have hinged on a candidate's position on the fluoridation of water or on nuclear power, but these have been rare. Elections are usually fought over a variety of issues; technological policy has been but one, and usually a minor one at that. And even where a technological issue is at the center of a campaign, the voters' voices are heard only after a technology is already in place, as with referenda on nuclear power. There is virtually no popular input into whether or not completely new technologies should be developed. In this sense, democratic controls are at best reactive. 民主选择可以因为候选人在关键技术问题上的立场而被投票支持或反对。 曾经有的地方选举的核心议题是关于候选人在水氟化或核电方面的立场，但这种情况很少见。 选举通常是围绕各种问题展开的。 技术政策只是一个，且通常是次要的。 即使在竞选活动的核心是技术问题，也只有在技术已经到位后才能听到选民的声音，就像核能公投一样。 对于是否应该开发全新的技术，几乎没有普遍的意见。 从这个意义上说，民主控制充其量只是被动的。
Is it possible to have democratic control of technology that goes beyond these after-the-fact votes? In some ways, the advance of technology has increased the potential for democratic participation in government. Most importantly, the electronic media have heightened our awareness of political issues. It has often been remarked, for example, that the widespread protests against the Vietnam War were stimulated by the horrible realities of warfare appearing on television day after day. At the same time, however, exposure does not guarantee an enlightened response. As we have seen, the expansion of newspaper reading that was triggered by the invention of the steam-powered rotary press stimulated a great outpouring of jingo-ist sentiment and the fanning of imperialist ambitions in the United States. Finally, many critics have decried the present-day debasement of the political process by slickly produced advertisements for candidates and ballot initiatives. It thus seems that advances in communication technologies have had mixed consequences for the democratic process. The electronic media in general and the Internet in particular hold out the prospect of a more informed electorate, but the positive contributions of these media are often overwhelmed by the negative ones, just as happened with the rise of the popular press generations earlier. 除了这些事后投票之外，是否有可能对技术进行民主控制？ 在某些方面，技术的进步增加了民主参与政治的潜力。 最重要的是，电子媒体提高了我们对政治问题的认识。 例如，人们经常说，电视上日复一日地出现可怕的战争画面，刺激了对越南战争的广泛抗议。 然而，与此同时，暴露并不能保证一个开明的反应。正如我们所看到的，由蒸汽驱动的轮转印刷机的发明引发的报纸阅读量的扩大，刺激了沙文主义情绪的大量涌现，并在美国煽动了帝国主义的野心。 最后，许多批评者通过为候选人和投票计划制作巧妙的广告来谴责当时政治进程的堕落。 因此，通信技术的进步似乎对民主进程产生了复杂的后果。 一般而言，电子媒体，尤其是互联网，让选民变得更加知情，但这些媒体的积极贡献往往被消极贡献所淹没，就像早先几代大众媒体的兴起一样。
Advances in electronic media have also presented the possibility of direct democracy through a kind of electronic town hall. Instead of delegating decisions to elected officials, every citizen could use an Internet site to vote on the pressing issues of the day. Such a system is certainly technologically feasible, but is it a practical possibility? Security questions aside, could voters be expected to be sufficiently well-informed to pass judgment on everything from levels of farm price supports to the wisdom of supplying arms to a revolutionary movement in some far-off land? And even if such a system were implemented, would it really result in a truly democratic order? It is obvious that people could not vote on every single issue, so some kind of rationing would have to be instituted. Some agency would have to determine what got on the "ballot" in the first place, and this would be a source of power in itself. The ability to set governmental agendas—the determination of which issues make it into the political arena—is a crucial political decision, and this system would do nothing to democratize this process. All voters could do would be to make choices according to a preplanned agenda. 电子媒体的进步也为利用线上市政平台实现直接民主提供了可能性。 每个公民都可以使用互联网站点对当今的紧迫问题进行投票，而不是将决策委托给民选官员。 这样的系统在技术上当然是可行的，但它是一种实际的可能性吗？ 抛开安全问题不谈，我们能否指望选民有足够的信息来判断从农产品价格支持水平到军备武器，再到某些遥远土地上的革命运动的一切？ 即使这样的制度得到实施，它真的会塑造一个真正的民主秩序吗？ 很明显，人们不可能对每一个问题都进行投票，因此必须实行某种分配制度。一些机构首先必须确定"选票"上的内容，而这本身就是权力的来源。 制定政府议程的能力——决定哪些问题进入政治舞台——是一项关键的政治决定，而这个制度对这个过程的民主化毫无帮助。 所有选民能做的就是根据预先计划好的议程做出选择。
Given the limitations of direct democracy, we necessarily have to rely on some form of representative democracy. Unfortunately, the established institutions of representative democracy in the United States have not always guided technological development in ways that serve the public interest. The key political actors have been especially responsive to large, well-organized bodies, such as industries, labor unions, and other special interests. All too often the common good is lost to the special pleadings of these groups. Compounding the problem is the fact that the political process is fragmented, which allows government agencies and officials to cut deals with special interests while no one looks after the needs and concerns of the nation as a whole. Under these circumstances, government officials end up representing themselves and their powerful constituents rather than the people who voted them into office. 鉴于直接民主的局限性，我们必然要依赖某种形式的代议制民主。 不幸的是，美国的代议制民主制度并不总是以服务于公共利益的方式激发技术发展。 主要的政治活动者对大型、组织良好的团体特别敏感，例如工业、工会和其他特殊利益团体。 这些群体的特殊诉求常常使共同利益丧失。 使问题更加复杂的是，政治进程是支离破碎的，这使得政府机构和官员可以与特殊利益相关者达成交易，而没有人关心整个国家的需求和关切。 在这种情况下，政府官员最终代表的是他们自己和他们强大的金主，而不是投票给他们上任的人。
Does this mean that there is no hope that individual citizens can affect the course of technological change? Despite what has just been said, there is some room for optimism, and there are numerous occasions when democracy can assert itself in technological affairs. Democracy may work best when issues are close to home. To note two recent examples, concerns about their effects on local environments have motivated well-organized protests over fracking and the construction of an oil pipeline passing through the Midwest. In contrast, many pressing but seemingly far-off technological issues do not engage the interest of people distracted by their individual problems of raising a family, meeting mortgage payments, or studying for exams. Burdened with mundane daily problems, it is all too easy for us to deny that there is an urgent need to do something about nuclear proliferation or climate change. The perception that immediate, local concerns are being affected by technological change can therefore energize greater levels of public perception than is the case when the issues seem too large and remote to concern us. There is considerable wisdom in the slogan that enjoins us to "think globally and act locally." 这是否意味着公民个人没有希望影响技术变革的进程？ 尽管刚才说了这些，但仍有一些乐观的余地，而且在很多情况下，民主可以在技术事务中发挥作用。 当问题离家很近时，民主可能会发挥最佳作用。 举两个最近的例子，因对当地环境影响的担忧引发的对水力压裂和穿过中西部的石油管道建设的组织良好的抗议。相比之下，许多紧迫但看似遥远的技术问题并没有引起人们的兴趣，他们因养家糊口、支付抵押贷款或学习考试等个人问题而分心。 背负着平凡的日常问题，我们很容易否认迫切需要对核扩散或气候变化采取行动。 因此，与问题看起来太大而遥远而无法关注我们的情况相比，技术变革正在影响直接的本地问题的看法可以激发更高水平的公众看法。 "放眼全球，本土行动"的口号中蕴含着相当多的智慧。
It must be admitted that local politics is uninteresting to many people, as the usually low levels of voter turnout for local elections attest. Moreover, participation at the grassroots level faces the same limits as other kinds of political participation; involvement can be time-consuming and stressful, and people would prefer to leave the tasks of governance to local officials. But at the same time, involvement in technological policies that have a direct impact on one's own community can reduce apathy and lethargy. And it might also be the case that expanding democratic participation and tying technological issues to local concerns would result in the emergence of technologies significantly different from those produced by our present system. 必须承认，地方政治对许多人来说是无趣的，因为地方选举的选民投票率通常很低。 此外，基层参与与其他类型的政治参与面临着同样的限制； 参与可能既费时又费力，人们更愿意将治理任务交给地方官员。 但与此同时，参与对自己社区有直接影响的技术政策可以减少冷漠和嗜睡。 也可能是扩大民主参与和将技术问题与当地问题联系起来会导致出现与我们现有系统产生的技术截然不同的技术。
Finally, while our governmental structures and processes have produced some technologies of very questionable value, we should also realize that no system of guiding technology will guarantee a utopia. No matter how advanced or benign our technologies, human life will always have its insecurities, disappointments, and tragedies. It can even be argued that it is dangerous to seek perfection in both our technological and political systems. There is something inhuman about a society that cannot tolerate the fact that life does not always go according to plan. The invention and development of new technologies have been characterized as ongoing searches for the "best way," and elegantly satisfactory solutions to technological problems do emerge on a regular basis. But most of life is not like that. We will always have to reconcile ourselves to the fact that even the most advanced and responsive technologies will not solve many of our basic problems. As we have seen, the spectacular advances of many individual technologies should not blind us to the fact that some of the inherent difficulties of life are simply not amenable to technological solutions. 最后，虽然我们的政府结构和流程产生了一些价值非常存疑的技术，但我们也应该意识到，没有任何指导技术的系统乌托邦。 无论我们的技术多么先进或良性，人类生活总会不安、失望和悲剧。 甚至可以说，在我们的技术和政治体系中寻求完美是危险的。 一个社会无法容忍生活并不总是按计划进行的事实，这是不人道的。新技术的发明和发展被描述为对"最佳方式"的持续探索，并且定期出现技术问题的优雅令人满意的解决方案。 但是生活中的大部分时间都不是这样。 我们将始终不得不接受这样一个事实，即即使是最先进和响应迅速的技术也无法解决我们的许多基本问题。 正如我们所见，许多个别技术的惊人进步不应让我们忽视这样一个事实，即生活中的一些固有困难根本无法通过技术解决方案来解决。
The Challenges of the Future 未来的挑战
In considering the years ahead, it is well to recall the waggish statement that it's dangerous to make predictions, especially about the future. The course of technologicaldevelopment has produced many surprises, and it will continue to do so. Fifty years ago few would have foreseen the emergence of smartphones with the power of existing mainframes. Yet at about the same time it was confidently predicted that nuclear generating plants would produce electricity "too cheap to meter." Forecasting is a highly inexact art, and although it can be safely said that our lives will be strongly influenced by technological change, predictions beyond this general statement are fraught with hazards. 在预测未来几年时，最好回想一下预测的危险性，尤其是对未来的预测。 技术发展的过程中产生了许多惊喜，而且还会继续如此。 五十年前，很少有人能预见到具有现有大型机功能的智能手机的出现。 然而，大约在同一时间，有人自信地预测，核电站将生产"太便宜而无法计量"的电力。 预测是一门高度不精确的艺术，虽然可以肯定地说，我们的生活将受到技术变革的强烈影响，但超出这一一般陈述的预测充满了危险。
Even so, the general contours of future technological developments can be discerned. Advances in transportation and electronic communication will bring the people of the world even closer together. The Internet will be the basis for ever-increasing amounts of information, media presentations, and social interaction. Advances in nanotechnology, materials, and microprocessors will produce fundamental changes in the design and operation of many objects. The application of artificial intelligence could affect every aspect of work, play, and learning. And genetic engineering might allow nothing less than the redesign of human beings. Profound social changes will be necessary if we choose to make use of these technologies. 即便如此，未来技术发展的总体轮廓还是可以看出的。 交通和电子通讯的进步将使世界人民更加紧密地联系在一起。 互联网将成为不断增加的信息量、媒体展示和社交互动的基础。 纳米技术、材料和微处理器的进步将对许多物体的设计和操作产生根本性的变化。 人工智能的应用可以影响工作、娱乐和学习的方方面面。 基因工程可能会对人类进行重新设计。 如果我们选择使用这些技术，就必须进行深刻的社会变革。
And yet, just because these things are possible does not mean that they should be done. We don't have to resign ourselves to the inexorable advance of technology while passively hoping that it produces more good than harm. Technology remains a human creation, and we have it in our power to determine its future course. Unfortunately, the power to make this determination is very unevenly distributed through society. A major reason for this unequal distribution of power is the unequal distribution of knowledge. This is especially unfortunate because a knowledgeable citizenry has always been essential to the functioning of democracy. In the words of Thomas Jefferson, "If we think [the people] not enlightened enough to exercise their control with a wholesome discretion, the remedy is not to take it from them, but to inform their discretion." The expansion of citizens' knowledge is even more crucial than it was in the days of Jefferson, when most adults worked as farmers and humans had never traveled faster than the speed of a horse. The relentless advance of technology has produced a dizzying pace of change that at times leaves us gasping. Even so, it bears repeating that technology is our own creation, and that its ultimate source is knowledge. But for technology to be truly beneficial, more than technical knowledge is required. Our challenge will be to develop and apply many different kinds of knowledge—ethical, philosophical, sociological, political, and economic—so that we can do a better job of defining our real needs and creating the technologies that serve them. 然而，仅仅因为这些事情是可能的并不意味着他们应该去做。 我们不必让自己屈服于无情的技术进步，而被动地希望它产生的好处多于伤害。 技术仍然是人类的创造，我们有能力决定其未来的发展方向。 不幸的是，做出这一决定的权力在整个社会中分布非常不均衡。 造成这种权力分配不均的一个主要原因是知识分配不均。 这尤其令人遗憾，因为知识渊博的公民一直对民主的运作至关重要。 用托马斯杰斐逊的话来说，"如果我们认为 [人民] 不够开明，无法以健康的自由裁量权来行使他们的控制权，那么补救措施不是从他们那里夺走它，而是告知他们的自由裁量权。"公民知识的扩展甚至比杰斐逊时代更为重要，当时大多数成年人从事农业工作，而人类的旅行速度从未超过马的速度。 技术的无情进步产生了令人眼花缭乱的变化步伐，有时让我们喘不过气来。 即便如此，还是有必要重申技术是我们自己的创造，其最终来源是知识。 但要使技术真正受益，需要的不仅仅是技术知识。 我们的挑战将是开发和应用许多不同类型的知识——伦理、哲学、社会学、政治和经济——以便我们能够更好地定义我们的真正需求并创造服务于他们的技术。
I hope that this book has given you some of the knowledge necessary to participate in shaping a future that will be strongly influenced by the technological decisions we make. But acquiring knowledge is not enough; it is also necessary to apply that knowledge. And that will be up to you. 我希望本书为您提供了参与塑造未来所必需的一些知识，而未来将受到我们所做的技术决策的强烈影响。 但是仅仅获得知识是不够的； 还必须应用这些知识。 这取决于你。
