Food security is a situation that exists when all people, at all times, have physical, social and economic access to sufficient, safe and nutritious food that meets their dietary needs and food preferences for an active and healthy life 粮食安全是指所有人在任何时候都能在物质、社会和经济方面获得充足、安全和有营养的食物，以满足其积极健康生活的饮食需求和食物偏好
Introduction 介绍
After 30 years of stable and at times falling food prices, the world was confronted in the second half of the 2000s with record-breaking food prices. Soaring food costs causing widespread hardship and scarcity were so severe in 2007 that riots and protests broke out in 30 countries around the world: in Mexico, demonstrators protested against the four-fold increase in the price of flat corn; Italy went on a one-day strike in September because of the price of pasta; and in West Bengal, food riots broke out in response to food rationing. 在经历了 30 年稳定并时而下降的粮食价格之后，世界在 2000 年代后半期面临着破纪录的粮食价格。 2007 年，粮食成本飙升导致普遍供销短缺，这造成了全球超过 30 个国家的骚乱和抗议：在墨西哥，示威者抗议扁玉米价格上涨了四倍； 由于意大利面价格上涨，意大利在 9 月份进行了为期一天的罢工； 在西孟加拉邦，人们因食物配给而爆发了骚乱。
At its peak, the international community was confronted with a confluence of global trends and events which were driving the prices ever upward. A High Level Conference on World Food Security convened by the UN's Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO) in June 2008 focused on the causes, consequences and solutions to this latest major threat to global food security. Was the world entering a new phase of food supply uncertainty? If so what were the contributing factors? How should the world respond? How were climate change and the demand for bioenergy crops affecting food supplies? 在最严重时期，国际社会面临着推动价格不断上涨的全球趋势和事件的累加。 联合国粮食及农业组织 (FAO) 于 2008 年 6 月召开了世界粮食安全高级别会议，重点讨论了这一全球粮食安全面临的最新重大威胁的原因、后果和解决方案。 世界是否进入了粮食供应不确定的新阶段？ 如果是，影响因素是什么？ 世界应该如何回应？ 气候变化和对生物能源作物的需求如何影响粮食供应？
Four years on, food price volatility persists. In their latest report on global food insecurity, FAO attempts to ask the question whether this volatility in food prices will continue into the future. Its conclusion is that as populations continue to rise and economic prospects improve, there will be a pressure on demand leading to increased prices. In addition, FAO warns that a range of other factors will combine to create a complex situation contributing to the volatility. For example, if the frequency of extreme weather events increases, interruptions to food production in key producing countries will be more frequent. Oil price increases can also increase the attractiveness of biofuel alternatives which in turn will also contribute to raising food prices. 四年过去了，食品价格波动仍然存在。 在其关于全球粮食威胁的最新报告中，粮农组织试图提出这样一个问题，即粮食价格的此类波动是否会持续到未来。 其结论是，随着人口持续增加和经济前景改善，需求压力将导致价格上涨。 此外，粮农组织警告说，一系列其他因素将结合起来，造成导致价格波动的复杂情况。 例如，如果极端天气事件的频率增加，主要生产国的粮食生产中断将更加频繁。 油价上涨会增加生物燃料替代品的吸引力，这反过来也将推高粮食价格。
Overall, while the extent of future increases and their underlying causes cannot be forecast with great reliability, what is known is that the risks of volatility are serious enough to ensure that food insecurity remains a high profile priority on the international community's agenda. 总体而言，虽然无法非常可靠地预测未来增长的程度及其根本原因，但众所周知，波动的风险非常严重，足以让粮食威胁继续成为国际社会的重点优先事项。
From the circumpolar perspective, this persistent volatility in global food prices is significant because it serves to highlight a range of developments and trends which are impacting on Inuit access to affordable and nutritious foods - both traditional foods as well as store bought goods. Food security in the Arctic has been a longstanding issue and has its genesis in a range of driving factors - not just cost. These include geography, pollution of country foods by contaminants, the impact of climate change and economic vulnerability. 从极地角度来看，全球食品价格的这种持续波动意义重大，因为它凸显了一系列影响因纽特人获得负担得起的营养食品——传统食品和商店购买的食品——的发展和趋势。 北极地区的粮食安全是一个长期存在的问题，其根源在于一系列因素——且不仅仅是成本。 这其中包括地理、污染物对乡村食品的污染、气候变化的影响和经济脆弱性。
This paper provides a summary of the issues which contribute to food insecurity for Inuit living in Alaska, Canada, Greenland and Russia (Chukotka). It also looks at food security from the perspective of the human right for Inuit to access adequate food - whether traditionally harvested or obtained commercially.It has been written by the Inuit Circumpolar Council (ICC) Canada to support the work of the ICC's Circumpolar Inuit Health steering committee in its advising and advocacy role to advance the health and wellbeing of Inuit living across the Arctic. 本文概述了导致居住在阿拉斯加、加拿大、格陵兰和俄罗斯（楚科奇）的因纽特人粮食威胁的问题。 此外，本文还从因纽特人获得充足食物（无论是传统收获的还是商业获得的）的人权的角度来看待粮食安全。 本文由加拿大因纽特人极地委员会 (ICC) 编写，以支持 ICC 极地因纽特人健康指导委员会的工作，发挥其建议和宣传作用，以促进生活在北极地区的因纽特人的健康和福祉。
The Inuit are an indigenous people totaling about 160,000 and living in four countries across the Arctic - Canada, Greenland, USA (Alaska) and Russia (Chukotka). The ICC was founded by Inuit leaders in 1977 to strengthen unity among Inuit living across the Arctic and to promote Inuit rights and interests on an international level. 因纽特人总共约有 160,000 人，他们生活在北极地区的四个国家——加拿大、格陵兰、美国（阿拉斯加）和俄罗斯（楚科奇）。 ICC 由因纽特人领导人于 1977 年成立，旨在加强生活在北极地区的因纽特人之间的团结，并在国际层面促进因纽特人的权益。
Global factors affecting food security 影响粮食安全的全球因素
Since 2005, a number of factors have combined to bring about a sharp increase in prices across a range of food and feed staples. While steep and often short-lived price increases had occurred in previous decades, the situation has been marked by substantial and simultaneous hikes across a broad range of commodities. By 2008, the international prices of all major food commodities had reached in real terms the highest they have been in 30 years. By 2010, the volatility varied between the commodities with world prices for wheat and maize doubling in the second half of 2010 and and the first half of 2011 while rice prices were relatively stable after a tumultous period of price rises in 2007. 自 2005 年以来，多种因素共同导致了一系列食品和饲料的价格急剧上涨。 虽然在过去几十年中出现了急剧且短暂的价格上涨，但这种情况的特点是广泛的大宗商品同时大幅上涨。 到2008年，所有主要粮食商品的国际实际价格均达到30年来的最高水平。 到2010年，小麦和玉米的世界价格在2010年下半年和2011年上半年翻了一番，而大米价格在经历了2007年价格动荡的上涨期后相对稳定。
No one factor is responsible for this development. Instead, a range of drivers has evolved to produce these results. According to FAO and the World Health Organization (WHO), these factors are: 没有任何一个原因对这一发展负责。 相反，一系列驱动因素已经演变为产生这些结果。 根据粮农组织和世界卫生组织 (WHO) 的说法，这些因素是：
Rapidly increasing fuel prices with a dual impact: increasing the cost of production and increasing the cost of distribution. 快速上涨的燃料价格具有双重影响：增加生产成本和增加分销成本。
Extreme weather in major cereal producing countries including extended droughts in Australia and Canada in the second half of the 2000s led to a fall in wheat yield by about a fifth driving up wheat prices by nearly 100 per cent; wheat crop damage in the Russian Federation at the start of the next decade and poor conditions for maize in the USA . Reduction in the global level of cereal stocks as the increase in demand has been gradually outstripping supply particularly since 2005. 主要谷物生产国的极端天气，包括 2000 年代后半期澳大利亚和加拿大的长期干旱，导致小麦产量下降约五分之一，並使得小麦价格上涨近 100%； 下一个十年伊始，俄罗斯联邦的小麦作物受损，而美国的玉米长势不佳。 随着需求的增加，全球谷物库存水平的下降已逐渐超过供应，特别是自 2005 年以来。
Growth in demand for biofuel commodities: A major impact on global markets as producers switch to commodities suitable for the emerging biofuel markets (sugar, palm oil, maize, cassava) resulting in decreased production of other food commodities. This has also been encouraged by legislation in some of the world's biggest farming nations e.g. five per cent of vehicle fuel in the USA must be ethanol. 对生物燃料的需求增长：随着生产商转向适合新兴生物燃料市场的商品（糖、棕榈油、玉米、木薯），全球市场受到了重大影响，导致其他食品商品的产量下降。 世界上一些最大的农业国家的立法也鼓励了这一点，例如在美国，5% 的车辆燃料必须是乙醇。
Growing demand for food by emerging economies: Income growth, particularly in India and China, is leading to changing demands for different food commodities away from starchy foods towards meat and dairy products. However, some observers believe that while this is an important trend, it is not the main cause for the current price hikes. 新兴经济体对食品的需求不断增长：收入增长，尤其是在印度和中国，正在导致对不同食品商品的需求发生变化，从淀粉类食品转向肉类和乳制品。 不过，也有观察人士认为，虽然这是一个重要趋势，但并不是当前价格上涨的主要原因。
Climate change impact on agriculture, fisheries and wildlife harvesting. It is recognized that the anticipated extreme weather events resulting from climate change will have increasingly negative consequences for agriculture and fisheries in all regions. This includes the movement of plant pests, animal diseases and invasive alien aquatic organisms. 气候变化影响农业、渔业和野生动物捕捞。 人们认识到，气候变化导致的可预见的极端天气事件将对所有地区的农业和渔业产生越来越多的负面影响。 这包括植物害虫、动物疾病和外来入侵水生生物的移动。
Separately, the World Economic Forum has recognized food security as a major area for international concern and response. In its 2012 Global Risks Report, a potential global food shortage crisis as well as a water supply crisis stand out as the two most important risks likely to threaten "the stability of modern civilization and the continued well-being of populations" and having "relatively high likelihood and potential impact in the next 10 years" In its earlier 2008 report, WEF had identified food security as "the nexus of a number of issues from energy security to climate change and water scarcity, may be emerging as one of the major risks of the 21st century. Long- and short-term drivers - population growth, changing lifestyles, climate change and the growing use of food crops for biofuels - may be shifting the world into a period of more volatile and sustained high prices. The consequences, particularly for the most vulnerable communities, may be harsh." 另外，世界经济论坛已将粮食安全视为国际关注和应对的主要领域。在其 2012 年全球风险报告中，潜在的全球粮食短缺危机和供水危机被列为可能威胁"现代文明的稳定和人民的持续福祉"的两个最重要的风险和具有"在未来 10 年内相对较高的可能性和潜在影响"。在其 2008 年早些时候的报告中，世界经济论坛将粮食安全确定为"从能源安全到气候变化和水资源短缺等一系列问题的交汇点，并可能正在成为 21 世纪的主要风险之一。长期和短期的驱动因素——人口增长、生活方式的改变、气候变化以及越来越多地使用粮食作物作为生物燃料——可能正在使世界进入一个更加不稳定和持续高价的时期。 其后果，尤其是对最脆弱的社区而言，可能是严重的。"
Food security for the Inuit 因纽特人的粮食安全
Against this backdrop of global trends in food security are the specific issues which have particular resonance for Inuit across the Arctic, although in varying degrees. The variations are due in part to the different economic and policy positions in each of the four countries that make up the Arctic Inuit homeland. Also settlement patterns vary across the Arctic. Results from the Survey of Living Conditions in the Arctic (SLiCA) showed that in Greenland, most indigenous people live in cities (places with populations over 10,000) or towns (populations between 1,000 and 7,000). In Chukotka and northern Alaska, most live in villages with populations less than 1,000. In Canada, most indigenous people live in towns. 在全球粮食安全趋势的背景下，北极地区的因纽特人尤其自身关心的特定问题，尽管程度不同。 这些差异部分是由于构成北极因纽特人家园的四个国家的经济和政策立场不同。 此外，整个北极地区的定居模式也各不相同。 北极生活条件调查 (SLiCA) 的结果显示，在格陵兰，大多数土著人居住在城市（人口超过 10,000 的地方）或城镇（人口在 1,000 至 7,000 之间）。 在楚科奇和阿拉斯加北部，大多数人居住在人口不足 1,000 的村庄。 在加拿大，大多数土著人居住在城镇。
Political and economic contexts aside, the impacts of climate change and the consequential effects on snow and ice are already being felt in small communities throughout the circumpolar north. Among the most significant of these impacts are "health and nutritional concerns (related to the availability of country food) associated with changes in the abundance and migratory patterns of subsistence resources." In other words, the food situation across the Arctic is increasingly affected by a range of extraneous factors whose effects are being felt very strongly at the local level. 撇开政治和经济背景不谈，整个北极圈的小社区都感受到了气候变化及其对冰雪的次生影响。 其中最重要的影响是"与生存资源丰富度和迁移模式变化相关的健康和营养问题（与国家粮食的供应有关）。" 换句话说，整个北极地区的粮食状况越来越多地受到一系列外来因素的影响，而当地对这些因素的影响非常强烈。
A paper by the Ajunnginiq Centre in 2004, Hunger in Inuit Communities, identified significant challenges facing Inuit families across Canada in accessing adequate nutritional food. Four years later, Canada's national Inuit organization, the Inuit Tapiriit Kanatami (ITK), hosted a workshop as part of its work in developing a national strategy on Inuit food security. Many of the issues identified at the workshop were similar to those set out in the earlier paper. And the issues impacting on Canadian Inuit are similar to those impacting on Inuit in other parts of the Arctic. The principal challenges to food security across the Arctic are: Ajunnginiq 中心在 2004 年发表的一篇论文《因纽特人社区的饥饿》指出了加拿大各地因纽特人家庭在获得充足营养食品方面面临的重大挑战。 四年后，加拿大的国家因纽特组织 Inuit Tapiriit Kanatami (ITK) 举办了一次研讨会，作为其制定因纽特人食品安全国家战略工作的一部分。 研讨会上确定的许多问题与早先文件中提出的问题相似。 影响加拿大因纽特人的问题与影响北极其他地区因纽特人的问题相似。 北极地区粮食安全面临的主要挑战是：
  • high cost often coupled with economic vulnerability;
  • decreasing consumption of country foods.
  • 高成本往往伴随着经济脆弱性；
  • 乡村食品的消费减少。
Exacerbating these challenges are major issues linked to: 加剧这些挑战的主要问题与以下方面有关：
  • contaminants and
  • climate change
  • 污染物和
  • 气候变化
High costs and economic vulnerability 高成本和经济脆弱性
Remoteness, limited transport infrastructure, difficult climatic conditions, high global prices for food commodities and oil all combine to make the cost of food and its distribution a significant driver of food insecurity for many Inuit communities. A price survey conducted by the Canadian department of Indian and Northern Affairs in 2006 and 2007 in 49 isolated northern communities showed that a food basket which would provide a nutritious diet for a family of four for one week costs between C$350 and C$450. The same basket cost between C$195 and C$225 in southern Canada. Subsequent surveys by the department in 2009 showed similar disparities between southern centres and the north.7 地处偏远、交通基础设施有限、气候条件恶劣、全球粮食商品价格和石油价格居高不下，所有这些因素共同使粮食成本及其分配成为许多因纽特社区粮食不安全的重要驱动因素。 加拿大印第安人和北方事务部于 2006 年和 2007 年在 49 个孤立的北方社区进行的一项价格调查显示，一个可为四口之家提供一周营养膳食的食品篮的成本在 350 至 450 加元之间。 在加拿大南部，同样的篮子成本在 195 至 225 加元之间。 该部门在 2009 年进行的后续调查显示，南部中心和北部之间存在类似的差异。
At the same time, families living in these remote communities also have to deal with the high cost of other essential commodities including oil, fuel and transportation essential for hunting activities. Confounding the position further are the low income levels, limited access to economic activities and the consequential dependence on social welfare which is often insufficient to cover basic living costs. 与此同时，生活在这些偏远社区的家庭还必须应对其他必需品的高昂成本，包括石油、燃料和狩猎活动所必须的运输工具。 进一步混淆这一立场的是低收入水平、有限的经济活动机会以及随之而来的对社会福利的依赖，这往往不足以支付基本生活费用。
While research and anecdotal evidence suggest that the high cost of living in the Arctic is a reality for many Inuit families, it is also true that the mixed economy based on both wage employment and harvesting is still important for circumpolar Inuit as demonstrated by the results of the SLiCA in Alaska and Greenland: 虽然研究和轶事等证据表明，对于许多因纽特人家庭来说，北极的高生活成本是现实，正如位于阿拉斯加和格陵兰的SLiCA 的结果所证明的那样，基于工资收入和狩猎的混合经济对于环北极因纽特人仍然很重要：
"In Alaska, most products of hunting, fishing, and gathering do not enter the market economy. Rather, subsistence products are directly consumed by the harvesting household, given away, or exchanged. Cash plays an important role in the Alaska mixed economy however. Money buys snow machines, gas, and ammunition. The time spent in wage work may conflict with time that otherwise would be spending harvesting subsistence resources. In Greenland, in contrast, licensed professional hunters account for a large portion of the harvest of traditional foods. Households purchase these products in local open-air markets or processed in supermarkets. Greenlandic households are, with some restrictions, also allowed to hunt and fish for the consumption of their own household. Despite differences in the structure of the mixed economy, these are measures of the extent to which the components of a mixed economy are present in the Arctic." "在阿拉斯加，狩猎、捕鱼和采集的大部分产品都没有进入市场经济。 相反，必需品由收获的家庭直接消耗、赠送或交换。 然而，现金在阿拉斯加混合经济中发挥着重要作用。 金钱可以购买造雪机、汽油和弹药。 花在有薪工作上的时间可能与原本用于收获生计资源的时间相冲突。 相比之下，在格陵兰，有执照的职业猎人占了传统食物收获的很大一部分。 家庭在当地露天市场购买这些产品或在超市加工。格陵兰家庭也可以为自己家庭的饮食而打猎和捕鱼，但有一些限制。 尽管混合经济的结构存在差异，但这些是衡量混合经济组成部分在北极存在的程度的方法。"
In a survey conducted in the Greenlandic community of Qeqertarsuaq in 2008, the community was found to have a mixed-subsistence, cash-based economy with residents undertaking both paid employment as well as traditional harvesting. Traditional foods were widely consumed and were a highly valued component of the diet. But the survey also showed that economic constraints limited access to traditional foods because of the high cost of fuel and other hunting expenses. Further to the high cost of fuel, "the cost of Greenlandic [traditional] food is influenced by supply, as determined by quota restrictions, environmental conditions and animal accessiblity" which increase the market value and reduce affordability. 2008 年在Qeqertarsuaq的格陵兰社区进行的一项调查发现，该社区是一种混合模式的、以现金为基础的经济，居民从事有偿就业和传统游牧活动。 传统食物被广泛食用，并且是饮食中非常有价值的组成部分。 但调查还显示，燃料和其他狩猎费用的高昂价格限制了传统食物的获取。 除了燃料成本高昂之外，"格陵兰[传统]食品的成本受供应影响，由配额限制、环境条件和动物可触及性决定"，这会增加市场售价并降低可负担性。
Decreased consumption of country foods 减少的乡村食品消费
While the findings on mixed economies operating across the Arctic point to the ongoing importance of country food consumption, data gathered in 2001 by the Kugaaruk Pilot Project under Canada's Food Mail program pointed to a general drop in the amount of country food included in the diet of those taking part in the survey although country food was available. 虽然关于北极地区混合经济体的调查结果显示出本地食品消费的重要性，但加拿大食品邮件计划下的 Kugaaruk 试点项目于 2001 年收集的数据表明，加拿大饮食中包含的本地食品数量普遍下降，尽管受调查者可以获得它们。
It has also been suggested that this trend away from country food is evident in Greenland. "Social pressures from outside, such as increased exposure to western lifestyles as a result of television and development of Arctic mineral resources, etc., and the associated increased availability of western foods and its promotion through advertising are all factors that contribute to a non-directed dietary change, moving away from nutritious traditional food towards a non-balanced westernized diet." A study in Alaska also pointed to a shift in Inuit diets towards an increased reliance on a western diet, although country foods were still regularly consumed with consumption varied with age, geographic location and season. 也有人提出这种远离乡村食物的趋势在格陵兰很明显。"来自外部的社会压力，例如由于电视和北极矿产资源的开发等而增加对西方生活方式的接触，以及相关的西餐供应增加和通过广告进行宣传都是导致非定向饮食改变的因素，从营养丰富的传统食品转向不均衡的西化饮食。" 阿拉斯加的一项研究还指出，因纽特人的饮食正在转向越来越依赖西方饮食，尽管乡村食物仍然经常食用，消费量因年龄、地理位置和季节而异。
In Russia, a different trend has emerged. During the Soviet era, Chukotka's Inuit were compelled to eat the ubiquitous and often mass produced Soviet food. The pressure was such that traditional foods were often only eaten in secret. Hunting rifles were discouraged in this Cold War region while collective enterprises such as fur farms and dairies were encouraged. Whales were no longer hunted by the locals but rather large government boats would catch gray whales and deliver them from village to village. A local hunter economy was replaced in a matter of two decades by a centrally-planned economy. 在俄罗斯，出现了不同的趋势。 在苏联时代，楚科奇的因纽特人被迫食用无处不在且大量生产的苏联食物。 政治压力是如此之大，以至于传统食物往往只能被秘密食用。 在这个冷战地区不鼓励使用猎枪，而鼓励运营毛皮农场和奶牛场等集体企业。 鲸鱼不再被当地人猎杀，而大型政府船只只会捕捉灰鲸并将它们从一个村庄运送到另一个村庄。 地方狩猎经济在二十年内被中央计划经济所取代。
The massive upheaval in the post Soviet era of the 1990s brought about widespread social pressures to include more Western European-style food in the Russian diet. But rather than move even further away from traditional foods during this post-Soviet period, there was a resurgence in popularity of traditional foods among the Inuit and lost skills were regained. But this resurgence was due largely to economic hardship. 1990 年代后苏联时代的大规模动荡带来了广泛的社会压力，要求在俄罗斯饮食中加入更多西欧风味的食物。 但是，在这个后苏联时期，传统食物并没有进一步远离因纽特人的餐桌，而是在因纽特人中重新流行起来，失去的技能又重新回来了。 但这种复苏主要是由于经济困难。
The increasingly difficult economic circumstances that the Chuktokans faced is summed up as follows: "According to official statistics, during the 1990s the real income in Chukotka was continually reduced and by 1999 it amounted to no more than 25% of the 1993 income value....By 2000, the indigenous population's purchasing power regarding foodstuffs was one-twelfth of what it was in 1985." Or as the report describes later, it was the food crisis in Chukotka that became one of the prime reasons for the resumption of hunting. 楚克托坎人面临的日益困难的经济形势概括如下："据官方统计，1990 年代楚科奇的实际收入不断减少，到 1999 年不到 1993 年收入的 25%...到 2000 年，土著居民对食品的购买力是 1985 年的十二分之一。" 或者正如报告后来描述的那样，楚科奇的粮食危机成为恢复狩猎的主要原因之一。
Contaminants 污染物
A complicating factor in the consumption of country food has been the presence of contaminants. Because of the remote location of the Arctic, it had previously been regarded as pristine. When Rachel Carson first described the detrimental impact of organochlorine pesticides on the environment in her book Silent Spring in 1962, she noted that "when scientists investigated the native diet of the Eskimos living [along the Arctic shores of Alaska] it was found to be free from insecticides. The fresh and dried fish; the fat, oil, or meat from beaver, beluga, caribou, moose, oogruk, polar bear, and walrus [...] all had so far escaped contamination." 乡村食品消费的一个复杂因素是污染物的存在。 由于北极地处偏远，以前曾被认为是原始的。1962 年，当雷切尔·卡森 (Rachel Carson) 在其著作《寂静的春天》(Silent Spring) 中首次描述有机氯农药对环境的不利影响时，她指出"当科学家们调查生活在 [阿拉斯加北极沿岸] 的爱斯基摩人的本地饮食时，发现它们不含杀虫剂。鲜鱼和干鱼； 迄今为止，海狸、白鲸、驯鹿、驼鹿、oogruk、北极熊和海象的脂肪、油或肉都没有受到污染。"
Twenty years later, researchers were surprised to find elevated levels of chemicals in blood and lipid tissues of indigenous populations in northern Canada, although possible emission sources were far away. It was found that the chemicals that were produced and used in the industrial regions of Europe, Russia, Canada and the USA had found their way into the Arctic food web, with the result that the formerly pristine diet of Inuit had become among the most contaminated. 二十年后，研究人员惊讶地发现加拿大北部土著居民的血液和脂质组织中的化学物质水平升高，尽管可能的排放源距离很远。他们发现了来自欧洲、俄罗斯、加拿大等的工业地区所生产并使用的化学品的痕迹。而在美国已经找到了它们进入北极食物网的途径，这导致因纽特人以前原始的饮食变成了最受污染的饮食之一。
Of particular concern was the way in which a wide spectrum of substances - persistent organic pollutants (POPs), heavy metals, and radionuclides - were reaching unexpectedly high levels in the Arctic ecosystem. The reason for these very high levels is linked to the special characteristics of the Arctic ecosystem. Marine mammals, which are a substantial part of the Inuit traditional diet, rely on fat reserves for energy and insulation against the cold. It is also a fact that the contaminants biomagnify up the food-chain. Most marine mammals are predators, and with each step up the food chain, the chemicals are more concentrated, until they reach the very high levels. Conversely, marine fish and animals which are lower down the food chain will have lower contaminant levels. POPs, because of their chemical properties, concentrate in fatty tissues and when consumed, the high levels of contaminants stored in these tissues are transferred to humans. The result is that in some parts of the Arctic, levels of contaminants in blood and breast milk are higher than those found anywhere else in the world. 尤其令人担忧的是，北极生态系统中各种物质——持久性有机污染物 (POP)、重金属和核辐射物——达到了出乎意料的高含量。 这样的高含量的原因与北极生态系统的特殊特征有关。 海洋哺乳动物是因纽特人传统饮食的重要组成部分，依靠脂肪储备来提供能量和抵御寒冷。 这也是污染物在食物链中向上生物放大的结果。大多数海洋哺乳动物都是食肉动物，随着食物链的上升，化学物质的浓度越来越高，直到达到非常高的水平。 相反，处于食物链下游的海洋鱼类和动物的污染物水平较低。 持久性有机污染物，由于其化学特性，集中在脂肪组织中，当被消耗时，储存在这些组织中的高浓度污染物会转移到人类身上。 这导致的结果是，在北极的某些地区，血液和母乳中的污染物含量高于世界其他任何地方。
In weighing up the very tangible health and cultural benefits of maintaining a traditional diet along side the negative consequences of moving away from traditional diets, health authorities throughout the Arctic support the continued consumption of traditional foods but also recommend an increased consumption of traditional products sourced from animals lower down the food chain and therefore less contaminated such as Arctic char. 为了在保持传统饮食的健康和文化益处以及远离传统饮食的负面后果之间取的平衡，整个北极的卫生当局支持继续消费传统食品，但也建议增加来自食物链下游动物的传统产品的消费，从而减少污染，例如北极红点鲑。
In the meantime, the international community has been working to reduce, and if possible eliminate, contaminant emissions. The European Community created the first international legally binding instrument aimed at reducing air pollution in 1979 in Geneva. The resulting Convention on Long-range Transboundary Air Pollution (LRTAP) entered into force in 1983. It has been extended by eight specific protocols, among them the Protocol on POPs and the Protocol on Heavy Metals, both of which entered into force in 2003. In 2001, with a strong role of the Canadian Government and aboriginal organizations (led by ICC), 114 countries signed the Stockholm Convention on POPs. 与此同时，国际社会一直在努力减少，并在可能的情况下消除污染物排放。 欧洲共同体于 1979 年在日内瓦制定了第一个具有法律约束力的国际文书，旨在减少空气污染。 由此产生的远距离越境空气污染公约 (LRTAP) 于 1983 年生效。 它已扩展了八项具体议定书，其中包括持久性有机污染物议定书和重金属议定书，两者均于 2003 年生效。 2001年，在加拿大政府和原住民组织（以ICC为首）的大力推动下，114个国家签署了关于POPs的斯德哥尔摩公约。
As a result of these efforts, it has been recently reported that levels of some contaminants in the Arctic environment have been declining. But it has also been found by several studies that a number of contaminants (e.g. mercury and some newly emerging POPs) are not decreasing in the environment and need immediate international action. With the emergence of the new POPs, it is increasingly difficult to keep up with the changing threat of contamination. Difficulties include the development of new methods to reliably measure the new chemicals and to evaluate which chemicals need to be scanned for. Several thousand different chemicals are being continuously released into the environment and determining which ones are of particular concern and need to be monitored is a diffcult task. 由于这些努力，最近有报道称北极环境中某些污染物的水平一直在下降。 但多项研究也发现，环境中污染物（例如汞和一些新出现的持久性有机污染物）的数量并未减少，需要立即采取国际行动。 随着新的持久性有机污染物的出现，应对不断变化的污染威胁越来越困难。 困难包括开发新技术来可靠地测量新化学物质并评估需要扫描哪些化学物质。 数千种不同的化学物质不断地被释放到环境中，确定哪些是值得特别关注和监测的是一项艰巨的任务。
One of the major issues confronting Inuit in Chukotka is the limited monitoring and response by authorities to the address the extent of contamination in traditional foods. According to ICC Chukotka, there is a strong concentration of heavy metals and mercury in the fat of marine animals. Deer and water fowl have also been found to contain high levels of cadmium and mercury. The impact is particularly felt among families on lower incomes as they rely more on traditional foods for their diet. 楚科奇因纽特人面临的主要问题之一是当局在解决传统食品污染程度方面的监测和反应有限。 据 ICC Chukotka 称，海洋动物的脂肪中含有大量重金属和汞。 鹿和水禽也被发现含有高浓度的镉和汞。 收入较低的家庭尤其能感受到这种影响，因为他们的饮食更多地依赖传统食物。
Climate change 气候变化
Eating country foods is important not only because of their nutritional benefits but also because of the broader importance of harvesting in supporting traditional knowledge and skills. But climate change is having an increasing and significant impact on hunting. As the UN Permanent Forum on Indigenous Issues (UNPFII) was reminded at its seventh session 2008 when special rapporteurs, Aqqaluk Lynge, then President of ICC Greenland and now Chair of ICC, and Victoria Tauli-Corpuz, then chair of UNPFII, presented their report, Climate change, biocultural diversity and livelihoods: the stewardship role of indigenous peoples and new challenges: 食用乡村食品很重要，不仅因为它们的营养价值，还因为它们在维持传统知识和技能方面具有更广泛的重要性。 但气候变化对狩猎的影响越来越大。 正如联合国土著问题常设论坛 (UNPFII) 在 2008 年第七届会议中特别报告员、时任国际商会格陵兰岛主席、现任国际商会主席的 Aqqaluk Lynge 和时任 UNPFII 主席的 Victoria Tauli-Corpuz 在他们的报告《气候变化、生物文化多样性和生存：土著人民的管理作用和新挑战》提出的那样：
For more than 20 years, indigenous hunters and elders in the Arctic have reported changes in their environment. Hunters speak of thinning sea ice that makes hunting much more dangerous, changes to permafrost that alter spring run-off patterns, a northward shift in seal and fish species, and rising sea levels with more extreme tidal fluctuations. They report that species they rely on are disappearing and that hunting routes near shorelines have disappeared due to erosion brought on by the thawing of permafrost. Villages have experienced increased flooding in winter due to lessened or disappearing pack ice that normally protects shorelines. 20 多年来，北极的土著猎人和长者报告了其生存环境发生的变化。 猎人说海冰变薄使狩猎变得更加危险，永久冻土的变化改变了春季径流模式，海豹和鱼类物种向北移动，以及海平面上升和更极端的潮汐波动。 他们报告说，他们赖以生存的物种正在消失，并且由于永久冻土融化带来的侵蚀，海岸线附近的狩猎路线已经消失。 由于往常保护海岸线的浮冰减少或消失，村庄在冬季经历了洪水泛滥。
Traditional hunters interviewed for ICC's report, The Sea Ice is Our Highway reported that they had to travel further to access wildlife. Formerly safe travel routes had become insecure due to a warming climate and melting ice. Wildlife habits and migration routes were changing. 接受 ICC 采访的传统猎人在报告说《海冰是我们的公路》说，他们必须走得更远才能接近野生动物。 由于气候变暖和冰雪融化，以前安全的旅行路线变得不安全。 野生动物的习性和迁徙路线正在发生变化。
In a 2009 UNEP/Grid-Arendal report, the authors note that climate change "poses a threat to country [traditional] food security in northern regions because it influences animal availability, human ability to access wildlife and the safety and quality of wildlife for consumption". They cite examples of higher winds making tavel and hunting more difficult and dangerous by boat in summer; the increased length of the ice-free season and decreased ice thickness making it more difficult and dangerous to access icedependent wildlife. 在 2009 年 UNEP/Grid-Arendal 的一份报告中，作者指出气候变化"对北部地区的国家（传统）粮食安全构成威胁，因为它影响了动物的供应，人类获取野生动物的能力，以及食用野生动物的安全性和质量"。他们列举了一些例子，风大使夏季乘船旅行和狩猎变得更加困难和危险； 无冰季节的延长和冰层厚度的减少使得接近依赖冰的野生动物变得更加困难和危险。
The 2008 survey conducted in Qeqertarsuaq, Greenland, also reported on the changes observed by local residents and the way in which animal availability and the ability to hunt and fish were closely linked with environmental conditions. 2008 年在格陵兰 Qeqertarsuaq 进行的调查还报告了当地居民观察到的变化，以及动物的可获性和捕捞能力与环境条件之间如何紧密连接起来。
The Inuit right to food security 因纽特人的粮食安全权
Food security is inextricably linked to a person's ability to exercise his or her right to food. That right is included in the 1948 Universal Declaration of Human Rights: "Everyone has the right to a standard of living adequate for the health and well-being of himself and of his family (sic) including food" (Article 25). It is also enshrined in the 1966 International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights. 粮食安全与个人行使其食物权的能力密不可分。 这项权利包含在 1948 年的《世界人权宣言》中："人人有权享受足以维持他本人和家人的健康和福祉的生活水准（原文如此），包括食物"（第 25 条）。 它也被载入了 1966 年的《经济、社会和文化权利国际公约》。
The UN's Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights (OHCHR) has recognized the importance of food security for indigenous peoples - not just from a calorific perspective but also from the broader socio-cultural perspective. In its paper on The Right to Adequate Food, the significance of food and its accessibility is acknowledged as being "inextricably grounded in …socio-cultural traditions and [the] special relationship to ancestral territories and resources. Food and its procurement and consumption are often an important part of their culture, as well as of social, economic and political organization. For Inuit, this linkage between food and culture is inextricable. 联合国人权事务高级专员办事处 (OHCHR) 已经认识到粮食安全对土著人民的重要性——不仅是从获取能量的角度，而且是从更广泛的社会文化角度。 在其关于充足食物的权利的论文中，食物及其可及性的重要程度被认为"与社会文化传统以及[与]祖先领土和资源的……不可分割的……特殊关系。 食物及其采购和消费通常是他们文化以及社会、经济、政治组织的重要组成部分。 对于因纽特人来说，食物和文化之间的这种联系是密不可分的。
Also important in the context of the right to food is the States obligation to protect the right to food. For Inuit across the Arctic, this is particularly relevant in terms of the level of chemically contaminated traditional foods. In this, OHCHR points out that States have to protect the right to food against against violations by third parties. "For example, States should prevent third parties from destroying sources of food by, for instance, polluting land, water and air with hazardous industrial or agricultural products or destroying the ancestral lands of indigenous peoples". As noted earlier, this area of contaminants is one in which ICC has taken a leading role internationally to bring about changes to international regulations and governance surrounding the production of contaminants which threaten the Arctic and its wildlife. 在食物权方面同样重要的是国家有义务保障食物权。 对于北极地区的因纽特人来说，这与传统食品受到化学污染的程度尤其相关。 在这方面，人权高专办指出，各国必须保护食物权免受第三方侵犯。 "例如，各国应防止第三方破坏食物来源，例如用危险的工业或农产品污染土地、水和空气，或破坏土著人民的祖传土地"。 如前所述，在这一污染物领域，ICC 在国际上发挥了主导作用，以改变有关威胁北极及其野生动物的污染物生产的国际法规和治理。
Responding to the challenge of food security and ICC's role 应对粮食安全挑战和ICC的作用
The food security situation for Inuit across the Arctic varies from community to community and is influenced by various factors. The development of effective strategies to address Inuit food security requires the close involvement of the communities affected as well as local and other authorities to ensure that the issues specific to the different locations are taken into account. 整个北极因纽特人的粮食安全状况因社区而异，并受到各种因素的影响。 制定解决因纽特人粮食安全问题的有效战略需要受影响社区以及地方和其他当局的密切参与，以确保考虑到不同地区的具体情况。
In considering food security in Inuit communities as a broader issue, it is important to remember that access to food isn't simply a technical issue. As spelled out clearly in the Rome Declaration which came out of the 1996 World Food Summit, there are integral links between food security and human rights. "Democracy, promotion and protection of all human rights and fundamental freedoms, including the right to development, and the full and equal participation of men and women are essential for achieving sustainable food security for all." 在将因纽特人社区的粮食安全视为一个更广泛的问题时，重要的是要记住，获得食物不仅仅是一个技术问题。 正如 1996 年世界粮食首脑会议发表的《罗马宣言》中明确指出的那样，粮食安全与人权之间有着不可分割的联系。 "民主、促进和保护所有人权和基本自由，包括发展权，以及男性和女性的充分和平等参与对于实现所有人的可持续粮食安全至关重要。"
Realization of this right to food is a responsibility shared by all, from families and communities through to national governments and international organizations. Existing national and regional responses to support that right include programs such as Canada's Northern Contaminants Program. National and state legislation which ensures Inuit with the appropriate rights to traditional hunting, fishing and gathering activities is another appropriate way to protect Inuit food security for nutritional, cultural and economic reasons. Similarly the international community has a responsibility to ensure indigenous rights are not nullified as a consequence of international agreements. 实现这一食物权是所有人的共同责任，从家庭和社区到国家政府和国际组织。 支持该权利的现有国家和地区响应包括诸如加拿大北方污染物计划之类的计划。 确保因纽特人对传统狩猎、捕鱼和采集活动享有适当权利的国家和州立法是出于营养、文化和经济原因保护因纽特人粮食安全的另一种适当方式。同样，国际社会有责任确保土著权利不会因国际协定而被取消。
It is in this area of promoting the Inuit right to food that ICC is in a position to play a particular role through its ongoing international advocacy work including in the UNPFII, UN Human Rights Council, Arctic Council, the International Whaling Commission and if feasible, appropriate FAO meetings. ICC already makes significant contributions in representing Inuit interests in international organizations tackling challenges including climate change and other environmental issues of pressing importance such as Arctic marine pollution and contaminants all of which are impacting on the Inuit right to food. 正是在促进因纽特人的食物权这一领域，ICC 能够通过其正在进行的国际宣传工作，包括在 UNPFII、联合国人权理事会、北极理事会、国际捕鲸委员会中发挥特殊作用，并在条件允许的情况下召开适当的粮农组织会议。ICC 已经在因其在国际组织中代表因纽特人利益的做出了重大贡献，以应对气候变化和其他紧迫的环境问题，如北极海洋污染和污染物，所有这些都影响因纽特人的食物权。
Another important contribution by ICC is the work undertaken to ensure that Inuit traditional knowledge is considered in the international efforts to underpin biodiversity particularly in the Arctic. The link between biodiversity and food security is well recognized and was reconfirmed in the 1996 Rome Declaration. ICC's work in the UN Convention for Biological Diversity (CBD) processes offers a valuable opportunity to contribute the Inuit knowledge and skills to the ongoing effort to conserve and protect biodiversity. A fundamental consideration in all of this work is that hunting is vital for Inuit not just for health and dietary reasons but also for the health of Inuit culture. ICC 的另一个重要贡献是确保因纽特人的传统知识在支持生物多样性的以北极地区为主的国际努力中发声的工作。 生物多样性与粮食安全之间的联系已得到普遍认可，并在 1996 年《罗马宣言》中得到再次确认。 ICC 在联合国生物多样性公约 (CBD) 进程中的工作提供了宝贵的机会，可以将因纽特人的知识和技能贡献给正在进行的保护生物多样性的努力。 所有这些工作的一个基本前提是尊重狩猎对于因纽特人来说至关重要的地位，这不仅是出于健康和饮食原因，而且是出于因纽特人文化的健康。
An important ICC activity linked to this is ICC Alaska's work with Alaskan Inuit communities. ICC Alaska has recently launched a new project "Building a Framework on How to Assess Food Security From an Inuit Perspective". Throughout this project ICC Alaska will work with Alaskan Inuit communities to identify the multi-faceted dimensions involved in food in/security. The finished framework will provide an overarching guidance on how to assess food security from an Inuit perspective, utilizing both Traditional Knowledge and Science. The finished product will be submitted to the Arctic Council with encouragement for the assessment to be conducted across the entire Arctic. Additionally, ICC Alaska and its membership have begun the process of approaching the US federal government to address food security co-management issues at this time. ICC 与此相关的一项重要活动是 ICC 阿拉斯加与当地因纽特人社区的合作。 ICC 阿拉斯加最近启动了一个名为"从因纽特人的角度构建如何评估粮食安全的框架"的新项目。 在整个项目中，ICC 阿拉斯加将与当地因纽特人社区合作，确定食品/安全所涉及的多方面维度。 项目完成的框架将为如何利用传统知识和科学从因纽特人的角度评估粮食安全提供总体指导。 成品将提交给北极理事会，并鼓励在整个北极进行评估。 此外，ICC 阿拉斯加及其成员目前已开始与美国联邦政府接洽，以解决食品安全共同管理问题。
Conclusion 总结
Food security or rather food insecurity continues to be a major priority for ICC's consideration and action. That action is undertaken on several fronts - through United Nations forums to push for frameworks and international legislation that regulate the production and distribution of contaminants; through international human rights bodies to ensure that the Inuit right to adequate food is protected; through regional and international environmental organizations to highlight the impact of climate change on the Arctic and its consequences for Inuit food security; and through national as well as international bodies to protect Arctic biodiversity which underpins Inuit health and wellbeing. As the international community's concerns about the future of global food security persist, so too does ICC's concerns about how this translates into the food security situation for Inuit across the Arctic. As a result, food security will remain a top priority for ICC action. 粮食安全或更确切地说，粮食不安全仍然是ICC考虑和行动的主要优先事项。 该行动是通过几个方面实行的——通过联合国论坛推动制定规范污染物生产和分配的框架和国际立法； 通过国际人权机构确保因纽特人获得充足食物的权利得到保护； 通过区域和国际环境组织强调气候变化对北极的影响及其对因纽特人粮食安全的影响，并通过国家和国际机构保护支撑因纽特人健康和福祉的北极生物多样性。 随着国际社会对全球粮食安全未来的担忧持续存在，ICC 对这如何转化为整个北极因纽特人的粮食安全状况的担忧也持续存在。 因此，粮食安全仍将是ICC行动的重中之重。
Contrast technological determinism with social constructivism as ways of interpreting the interaction of technological and social change.
  • technological determinism
    1. in which technological change is viewed as a largely self-contained process
  • social constructivism
    1. technological change is shaped by its surrounding social, economic, and political forces.
Briefly articulate the Great Breakthrough Thesis.
  1. The history of technology is often linked to single revolutionary inventions; e.g., penicillin; the light bulb; the airplane; the computer; etc.
  2. Technological breakthroughs are often connected to individuals often described as self-reliant geniuses; e.g., Alexander Fleming; Thomas Edison; the Wright brothers; Steve Jobs; etc.
  3. Entrepreneurs who take invention and convert it into a commercial success are also important, though less recognized than inventors themselves
  4. Despite the "Great Breakthrough Thesis", technological advances are often achieved in a painfully slow, gradual, incremental way
What does “R & D” stand for? How is “scaling up” related to R & D? Why is it an important part of technological advancement?
  1. R & D stands for Research and Development
  2. Large-scale production required development of new technology
    • Large-scale production required development of new technology
    • slow, unspectacular improvements are important for technological advancement
In what ways did Charles Babbage's computer provide a preview of today's computers? What ideas and/or parts of his computer exist in modern computers?
an “analytical engine” that contained a set of input devices, a processor, a control unit, memory storage, and an output mechanism
What were some of the late 20th century technologies that were essential to the survival of the internal combustion engine? Why was tetraethyl lead an important contributor to the improvement of internal combustion engines?
    1. use of microprocessors and computers for the regulation of spark advance and air-fuel ratios
    2. the spark was timed to occur before the piston reached the top of its stroke
    3. reshaping the combustion chamber and piston crown
    4. the addition of tetraethyl into fuel
  • the addition of tetraethyl led to gasoline allowed higher compression ratios and a subsequent improvement in both power and economy.
What were some of the products and production methods developed in the bicycle industry that were subsequently used by the emerging automobile industry?
  • products:
    • ball bearings
    • spoke wheels
    • drive chains
  • production methods:
    • turning, boring, drilling, milling, and planning
    • electrical resistance welding
    • use of stamped components
What do economists mean by effective demand? Belated demand? Why are some technologies considered to be “ahead of their time”? Give an example.
  • Level of demand that represents a real intention to purchase by people with the means to pay.
  • It has no clear immediate use, but if it succeeds at all, it needs more time to create its market.
  • Because these technologies were not fully recognized when they were first invented
  • The pneumatic tire was patented in 1845 and then forgotten until it was reinvented by John Dunlop in 1888.
Why did photographic portrait studios prosper during the second half of the 19th century?
the ascendance of the property-owning commercial and industrial bourgeoisie, who had a keen desire to flaunt their affluence by taking on characteristics of the old aristocracy. But many of the rising bourgeoisie lacked the money or the time for the painted portrait. Their aspirations were therefore met by the photographic portrait studio.
Does demand-pull affect revolutionary technology? Does it affect current technology gaining refinement? Why?
  • the very novelty of a revolutionary breakthrough makes it difficult to determine what its ultimate uses will be and who, if anyone, will want it. Therefore it is hard to be affected by the demand-pull
  • refinement can be affected by the demand-pull, because the basic technology is already in use, and there are likely to be people and business firms that want and are willing to pay for, the new wrinkles that promise to improve existing technology.
In what sectors of the economy are market forces of limited relevance for technological advance?
there are large sectors of the economy where prices and the costs of production are secondary concerns.
  • defense industry: where the presumed dictates of national security have allowed the deployment of staggeringly expensive military technologies
  • public health care: When faced with a choice between controlling medical expenses or saving lives and alleviating pain through the use of sophisticated technologies, it is difficult for any individual or society concerned with the well-being of its members to put the former ahead of the latter.
Why do centrally planned economies have a poor record of fostering technological advance?
Centrally planned economies rest on the assumption that economic activities can be reduced to predictable routines. But the course of technological innovation is notoriously difficult to predict.
Why is a market economy particularly effective in stimulating technological advance?
  1. market economy promises financial rewards to those able to meet the needs of consumers
  2. market economy is characterized by the presence of numerous competitors
  3. market system is particularly effective in eliciting the production of the auxiliary items necessary for technological innovation
What is meant by “cultural lag”?
cultural lag : Technology moves ahead, but many other things lag behind
What are some of the deficiencies of the theory of cultural lag?
  1. technological changes are simply taken as givens, and no attempt is made to delineate how they came to be in the first place.
  2. many attempts to demonstrate the connection between technological and social changes present us with the problem of measuring and trying to connect different kinds of phenomena.
  3. something other than the technology itself is affecting the extent of and speed at which particular cultural lags are eradicated.
  4. the theory of cultural lag assumes a unified society and culture and ignores the economic, political, and cultural divisions to be found in all complex societies.
  5. The hidden value judgment implicit in it is the notion that technology is a progressive, dynamic element in human history, and that social and cultural arrangements are intransigent sources of obstruction.
What are the assumptions of Convergence Theory?
convergence theory argues that the nations of the world are becoming more similar to one another—that is, they are converging—as they make use of the same technologies.
What are some of the technologies that are used for different purposes and in different ways around the globe?
  1. television in the United States as well as much of the world is primarily geared toward entertainment and the desire of advertisers to persuade the viewing public to buy their products. authoritarian states have used television to trumpet the achievements of their regime, and a great deal of programming consists of stories that glorify the political leadership
  2. cars throughout the world use the same set of technologies and are similar in the layout of their controls. But as anyone who has driven outside his or her native land will attest, driving styles can vary greatly from place to place.
Identify the reasons why engineers have had a hard time converting their knowledge into power.
“knowledge explosion” has made all of us relative ignoramuses. Even well-trained scientists and technicians have to admit their own limitations when they leave their own field of specialization.
Why are technical issues often not solved on the basis of purely technical considerations?
Their social consequences have to be considered, and when this happens, value judgments often have to be made. These judgments necessarily take the expert well outside the realm of his or her expertise.
Who was Thorstein Veblen and what was his prescription for the governance of a technologically advanced society?
  • He is a sociologist/economist who expounded his ideas on technocracy, the exercise of political authority by engineers and other technical experts.
  • He believes that the only solution of the greatest obstacle to continued economic progress was a takeover of business enterprises by a “Soviet of Technicians” so that the economy would be continuously stimulated by technological advances instead of being retarded by the narrow financial interests of absentee owners and their delegated managers.
As formulated by John Kenneth Galbraith, what is the “technostructure”?
managers and engineers with the specialized knowledge and talent essential to planning and decision-making.
Why does the movement of engineers into managerial positions have the paradoxical result of reducing the influence and authority of engineers?
  1. For most engineers, success in one’s career means attaining a managerial position, not being an increasingly proficient engineer.
  2. The prospect of moving from engineering into management can affect a person’s values and undercut his or her identity as an engineer.
What is a “whistle-blower”?
A whistle-blower is someone who detects some sort of wrongdoing within his or her organization and brings it to the attention of the public.
How does the aftermath of the Challenger disaster illustrate the perils of being a whistle-blower?
  1. whistle-blowers face ostracization and isolation from their original organization.
  2. suffering from traumatic stress
  3. suffer considerable financial hardship and psychological strain
  4. The battle of an engineer against his or her organization is likely to be a lonely one.
According to Robert Blauner, how did different workplace technologies affect workers and the work that they did?
  • printing: high degree of worker skill and involvement: the absence of specialized machinery resulted in a work environment that allowed a great deal of worker autonomy
  • textile mill: machine-minders: activities had to be closely attuned to the demands of the equipment, so there was little room for individual initiative
  • automobile: assembly-line operations: forced the worker to submit to the rigid scheduling of activities that were dictated by the inexorable movement of the line
  • chemical manufacture or oil refining: made use of highly sophisticated technologies: work could not be precisely scheduled or regulated, and they enjoyed a considerable amount of on-the-job freedom
What did Joan Woodward's research reveal about the influence of different production technologies on organizational structures?
  • large-batch and mass production
    1. required routinized processes, narrowly defined job duties, and a clear hierarchy of authority that kept a firm grip on things
    2. Managerial specialization occurred more frequently
  • process production
    1. regular flow of worker-management communication
    2. required a higher ratio of managers to other personnel than was the case in organizations using different production technologies
  • unit and small-batch production
    1. regular flow of worker-management communication
According to Charles Perrow, what are the two aspects of work done within an organization that most strongly affect organizational structures and procedures?
  • the degree of variability of the raw materials processed by the organization
  • the extent to which problem-solving procedures can be routinized
Why is there no such thing as an optimal, universally valid organizational form?
Because the organizational structure should reflect the particular qualities of the raw materials being used and the technology used for their transformation. To be effective, an organization must use technologies appropriate to its tasks.
Why, according to David Noble, was record playback not used for the programming of machine tools?
Because with record-playback the control of the machine rests with the machinist, but with NC there is a shift of control to management.NC tools promised a reduction of the decision-making powers of workers and vested it with managers, engineers, and programmers.
How might modern information technology affect the work roles of workers and managers?
  • Modern information systems can be used to enhance the power and responsibilities of shop floor workers
    • computerized information systems can just as easily dilute managerial authority by making information more readily available to ordinary workers
    • computerized information systems may be used to empower workers, enhance their responsibilities, and give them a claim to higher wages
  • they can produce the opposite effect by giving management a greater capacity to centralize operations and restrict the discretion of the workers
    • technology can reduce dependency on operators with in-depth knowledge
    • technology may be employed because managers see it as a way of extending their own power
For what purposes are face-to-face communications superior to electronically mediated communications?
  • negotiating
  • maintaining relationships
  • building trust
In the automobile industry, how did impersonal, market-based relationships between OEMs and suppliers contribute to the decline of the industry in the 1970s and 80s?
  • The OEMs did not inform their suppliers about long-range intentions, and as a result, suppliers could not effectively plan for the future.
  • Research is done by suppliers usually took place without direct consultation with the OEMs, and the job of application came only after the component had been developed.
  • There were few attempts to foster joint efforts between OEM and supplier in order to devise and develop new technologies.
Why are large organizations essential for the promotion of technological advance?
  • It is admirably equipped for financing technical development
  • Large organizations are often better equipped to do development work, where scaling up and making relatively small but nonetheless crucial improvements are the key tasks
Under what circumstances does bureaucratic organization work well? Under what circumstances does it work poorly?
  • circumstances where bureaucratic organization work well
    • bureaucracies thrive on routine, working best in stable environments where nothing new comes along to disturb their machinelike operations
  • circumstances where bureaucratic organization work poorly
    • bureaucratic routines are difficult or impossible to reconcile with the inherent uncertainty of creating something new
Why may it be difficult to initiate and sustain entrepreneurial activities in many organizations?
  • bureaucratic routines are difficult or impossible to reconcile with the inherent uncertainty of creating something new
  • organizations may find it hard to accommodate employees who take on the role of entrepreneur
What was the first example of the U.S. federal government's efforts to encourage technological advance?
Article 1, Section 8, of the Constitution, stipulates that Congress is to "promote the Progress of Science and Useful Arts by securing for limited Times to Authors and Inventors the Exclusive Rights to their respective Writings and Discoveries."
How do patents encourage technological advance? How do they discourage technological advance?
  • How do patents encourage technological advances:
    1. The government's granting of patent rights provides the legal framework for technological advances generated by individuals and private organizations.
    2. Patents can bring profits to innovation
  • How do patents discourage technological advances:
    1. Revenues might undermine some of the basic values of scientific institutes
    2. Patent hinders the free transmission of knowledge
What is a "negative externality"? Give an example.
  • A technological change has created problems that are not borne exclusively by its owners
  • automobile: the operation of the car results in costs for the society as a whole: increased pollution, congestion, and so on. Since these costs are not included in the market transaction, governmental action is necessary.
Identify the various ways that the government affects technological change.
  • governments use Constitution to protect technological innovations
  • governments use patents to provide the legal framework for technological advances
  • governments at all levels do much to indirectly sponsor technological advances through their support of education
  • government programs also provide the auxiliary goods and services that are essential for the use of particular technologies
  • governments need to take action on the negative externalities caused by innovation
  • governments can also encourage the development and use of specific technologies by offering tax credits or deductions to those willing to invest in them
  • governments need to deal with the consequences of emerging technologies
  • governments are directly involved in the generation of some of these technologies through its support of research and development
What was the approximate distribution of government R&D funds for different energy sectors from 2003 to 2012? Does this breakdown tell us anything about the government's energy priorities?
from the fiscal year 2003 to 2012 the federal government spent a total of nearly $40 billion on energy R&D. Of that sum,
  • 25.4 percent went to fossil fuel R&D
  • 25.9 percent went to nuclear R&D
  • 16.4 percent went to energy efficiency R&D
  • 17.1 percent went to renewable energy R&D
What are the key agencies of the federal government that shape technology policies?
  • Presidential Science Advisory Committee (PSAC)
  • Office of Science and Technology Policy (OSTP)
  • Office of Technology Assessment (OTA)
What are some technological systems that work in close conjunction with federal and state governments?
the House Armed Services Subcommittee and the Senate Agriculture Committee
What was the Office of Technology Assessment? What happened to it? Why?
It had as its purpose the provision of information to Congress to help guide its decisions about technological policy, and to give it more leverage over the president in science and technology matters. OTA investigated a wide selection of topics that ranged from an examination of the physiological basis of drug addiction to an evaluation of the Social Security Administration's plans to upgrade its computer facilities.
How may "focusing events" shape future policies?
"focusing events" can grab attentions of government. This will fragment the approach to governing technological change, and make the decision-making loss of calm deliberation.
What is the "iron triangle"? How has it affected technology policy?
    1. congressional committees
    2. government agencies
    3. key groups whose interests are closely affected by governmental decisions
    • The decision to sponsor a new technology, along with the shape that it takes as it is developed, is often determined by these triangles.
    • This means that the government usually doesn't sponsor the development of new technologies as part of a general effort to find solutions to public problems.
    • Rather, technology is sponsored because a coalition can be formed from the members of the triangle, who see to it that the selected technologies develop in accordance with their own needs and interests.
According to Ernest Fitzgerald, what are the two phases of innovative military programs?
  1. It's too early to tell
  2. It's too late to stop
Why are efforts to democratize technological decisions often reactive in nature?
Most of us have been little more than the consumers of technologies that have been developed by people and organizations largely unknown to us.
How has the growth of the electronic media affected political processes in recent years?
  • electronic media have heightened our awareness of political issues.
  • electronic media in general and the Internet in particular hold out the prospect of a more informed electorate
  • electronic media have also presented the possibility of direct democracy through a kind of electronic town hall
How is "food security" defined? (p.2) What do you suppose "social" access means?
  • Food security is a situation that exists when all people, at all times, have physical, social and economic access to sufficient, safe and nutritious food that meets their dietary needs and food preferences for an active and healthy life
  • Social access to food. That some members of society suffer from malnutrition while others do not under the same conditions of physical and economic food accessibility is indicative of differential social access to food.
Identify several factors responsible for the recent upsurge in food prices around the world? (pp. 3-4) Of these factors, which one(s) have the greatest impact on the Inuit's access to "country foods" and traditional food harvesting activities? (pp. 4-5)
    1. Rapidly increasing fuel prices
    2. Extreme weather
    3. Reduction in the global level of cereal stocks
    4. Growth in demand for biofuel commodities
    5. Growing demand for food by emerging economies
    6. Climate change impact
    1. Rapidly increasing fuel prices
    2. Climate change impact
    3. Growth in demand for biofuel commodities
What is a "mixed economy"? (pp. 5-6) Why does money play such an important role in an economy which depends heavily upon locally harvested food (i.e., country food)?
  • An economy based on both wage employment and harvesting
  • Inut people use money to buy snow machines, gas, and ammunition
Has harvesting and consumption of country food among the Inuit increased or decreased (in general terms) in recent years? (p.6) Why?
  • Decreased
    • increased exposure to western lifestyles
    • increased availability of western foods and its promotion through advertising
  • In Russia, there was a resurgence in the popularity of traditional foods among the Inuit
  • Caused by the increasingly difficult economic circumstances
Identify a few examples of contaminants found recently in the country food of the Inuit. (pp. 7-8) Where do these contaminants come from? Have efforts to reduce contaminants in the traditional foods of the Inuit been successful? (p. 8)
    • the chemicals that were produced and used in the industrial regions had found their way into the Arctic food web, with the result that the formerly pristine diet of Inuit had become among the most contaminated.
    • in some parts of the Arctic, levels of contaminants in blood and breast milk are higher than those found anywhere else in the world.
  • industrial regions of Europe, Russia, Canada, and the USA
  • The conclusion of the report on the results of pollution control is still unclear: Some reports show that levels of some contaminants in the Arctic environment have been declining, but it has also been found by several studies that the number of contaminants are not decreasing
Identify the ways in which climate change is impacting on the harvesting activities of the Inuit. (pp. 8-9)
  • thinning sea ice makes hunting much more dangerous
  • changes to permafrost that alter spring run-off patterns
  • northward shift in seal and fish species
  • rising sea levels with more extreme tidal fluctuations
  • species they rely on are disappearing
  • hunting routes near shorelines have disappeared due to erosion brought on by the thawing of permafrost
  • Villages have experienced increased flooding in winter due to lessened or disappearing pack ice that normally protects shorelines
The authors state that "…the linkage between food and culture is inextricable." (p. 9) Looking back over the article, identify examples of this linkage.
  1. increased exposure to western lifestyles increased Inuit consumption of western food
  2. During the Soviet era, Chukotka's Inuit were compelled to eat Soviet food. This forced Inuit people to abandon their culture.
